O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine with its accomplishment, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its revelations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to all, thus the science has perished and decayed, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed and science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 Or it seems to me that I wish to revive the ordinance of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and brevity; and I will come with the forms of the cautery irons and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for the reason that no good masters of surgery are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And he who undertakes it must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and tendons and the number of them, and their movement and resting, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable in the aforementioned matters, let him beware lest he fall into error and harm people; as I have often seen many who engage in this science and abandon their own knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 Because I saw a foolish doctor who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of the neck; because of which so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another doctor who removed a stone from a man with water, and the stone was large; he took away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called for it to be drawn out, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if they cut into it, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another doctor take care of the Duke of our land, whose leg was broken and with the break he had an open wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, pressed the fracture onto the wound on both sides with great force, and left no flesh at all to the wound, and left it like this; and commanded that it should not be unbound; and so he stayed until the leg was completely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to come to him, and I hurried to go unbind the leg; and when I unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But still the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease spreading throughout the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another physician who cut open an abscess and then inflamed it due to the evil of his rule.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a chancre, when it is filled with melancholic humor, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can entirely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, work where there is danger in many ways; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos - For this reason it is necessary that you protect yourselves, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on a serious illness unless you are called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have composed this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and medicine cautery, and this chapter is arranged from the head to the feet; about the shapes of instruments, and about the tools for cauterizing, and about everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping and wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from the head to the feet, and about the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the nature and harmfulness of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the nature and harmfulness is the longest speech and most subtle science and secret response; and many of the wise have spoken about this, and they agree on it; but their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where there is material, except for two complexions: namely, hot complexion without material, and dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 In the hot and dry complexion together with material, some discuss and say that cautery is of great help there; and others say the opposite: that cautery does not benefit a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 Because the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat a hot illness with heat or drying; and he who says otherwise says that cauterization is of great help in treating hot and dry diseases in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 And yet, do not attempt this except for those who have proven it, and who know through long practice the chapter on cauterization, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and their outcomes and the duration of time; we should not fear other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases. ︎
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the doctors gathered and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that fire cautery is among the secrets of healing, and more effective than a burning medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not affect anything other than the member that is burned, unless there is little room for it to do so.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines pass from one member to another and cause disease in the sick member; and by chance they kill the patient. Fire, due to its high nature and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And thus have I found it through experience and the length of my service and study in this art, based on the truth of things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of this discourse, because I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that lies in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away bodily ailments, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed upon what time the cauteries should be done, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the harm that occurs is remedied by the help of cautery; and likewise if the cautery is necessary for pain, it must be done immediately and hastily so that the member does not await the time when greater evil may come.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And never think of it thus, dear son, as foolish physicians do; for the disease that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because cautery is nothing more than a medicine that changes the complexion, dries the humors that cause pain, and is more effective than medicine due to its swift action, and the virtue of its work and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its strength; and in him are gathered superfluities by the consumption of food and similar things, unless there are cauteries administered in the place where there is little superfluidity and moisture, such as tooth-cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are valuable after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in some diseases and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cautery with gold instruments is more effective than iron, and those outside the field said this only for the quality of gold and the height of its substance; but they were wrong because I have proven it, and found that it is true in some men; and cautery with gold is indeed more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 Yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; if heated too much, it burns in the fire; and thus there are many hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And because of this, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 I have organized this chapter from the head to the feet so that it will be easier to find the way.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is effective for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways to do it due to a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and due to excessive dreams and toothache and sore throat, and above all for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a dissolving medicine that cleanses the head three or four times, according to what the virtues and age and habit of the patient can endure; and then make the head of the patient sweat.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then make him sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands on a light weight; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and there where your middle fingers come together, let it bleed, and heat the cautery which is called "olivare," this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the designated spot, and in descending and tightening your hand bit by bit while turning; then lift your hand quickly, and check the spot if you see the bone one sole size small; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take a pouch of silk, and put soft cotton inside, and place on the spot, and let it stay for three days; afterwards put a damp cloth with butter; and leave it on until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon," until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And the ancients said that when the wound remains open longer, it purges more; therefore, they use movements.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that the cautery should be left on until part of the bone is burned; then scrape off what has been burned from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And the others said that one should leave the cautery on and press so hard that a piece of bone is removed as wide as a spindle, which women put in their distaffs, so that the humors flow out more easily; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should cure and sew it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some people where there is a sign of fear; and I think that I must leave it; for the head is weakened by continuous secretions of nature, as we see in other members; and also when the patient’s head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healthy and beneficial to me, I use that work therefore together with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When chronic pain comes over the whole head and lasts long, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, and oils and poultices; and if he undergoes the cautery that we have mentioned before and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize a little under that which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 Afterwards, make the cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place which is called "vasselz"; and there is the place where one puts cupping glasses; and raise your hand so that you cannot see up to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries of the horns must be more subtle than those used for the middle part of the head, and this is the procedure.
dou cautere dou chief	 Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the eye is purged with purging medicines, and other treatments are done as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then he makes cauteries according to two methods, that is to say with watery medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with watery medicine is such that you take a pod of garlic, and remove the skin and put it in two eyes, and then open the temple where the pain is so that you can place the pod of garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and compress it well and leave it like this for twelve hours; and then unbind and pull out the pod of garlic, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then apply a linen cloth soaked in butter until the pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 Après le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sané;
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Et quant il sera assez chaut, metes en li l'ung des deux poins dont je t'ai parle.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 Et si vint il assez chaut et ne te brusle les mains, si le met sor la plaie que tu veis.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 Et saches que li culterares ne doivent pas touchier l’os.
de emigraine	 Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you treat migraine as we have previously said in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery previously mentioned of medicine and iron is not sufficient for it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called «cultellare» until it is white; and thus on the painful spot, a line of half an inch in length, and remove your hand once, and hold so that you do not cut the artery and do not go as far as the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when one eats, and let the nerve have no regard for moving or spasm coming to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where there is great fear in cutting, and also for him who does not know about it, and who is not a student and experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how one stops blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you at the appropriate place in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, apply the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with a cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the ear pain due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from the cold, and one has worked with dissolving medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point", of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After piercing all around the unhealthy ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and you move away a bit above the root of the ear after having marked the place for incision; and have ten punctures around each ear; then treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torture that must be treated with cautery is not outside of those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not perform cautery on similar ones that come from drought and nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you treat this type of torture that moves from phlegm of the throat and cleansing of the head and gargling, and it does not help, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a bit outside the temple, and the third between the two lips; and place the cautery in the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery on the top of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery until half the head is burnt; this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it is similar to the cutler we mentioned earlier, but it is a little more subtle and requires the knife to be a little larger; after curing the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the place called "vassal" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the stomach’s opening; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	 of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, you must give the patient large pears and pills to cleanse the brain; afterwards, wash the entire head of the patient and place on the back of the head a plaster of mustard seed as described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, make III cauteries on the middle of the head descending to the neck, with a distance of I two between each cautery; and treat it as the others, and if you see it approaching, and the patient can endure it, make I cautery in the middle; and if necessary, II more on the two horns, and treat until it is healed; and let the cautery be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 from the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 The head should be purified of hair and of what we have said before; then anoint the patient's head, make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and I behind, and III on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can endure it, and the disease is gone, make IV cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and let the cautery be called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	 Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic must not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and first one must moderate the brain with years and other treatments which we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and capable of taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, one makes him gargle and chew to moderate the brain often with good food; afterwards raise his head in the middle, and there make a cautery as we have said before, and make a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is robust and can tolerate it, make the cauteries as I have said for one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the cautery in a subtle manner as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are superfluous or corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then use the same cautery as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if due to melancholy the superfluity inclines towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink that will purify his brain, according to what was said earlier in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After washing the patient's head, make a linen bandage well-shaped like a circle and place it on the head. And let the patient sit with legs crossed and be held firmly from all sides; then present the ointment, which consists of the juice of old sheep’s butter mixed with burnt wine; and heat it gently over a moderate fire so that the fingers can touch it without burning. Afterward, remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool down; and do this for the patient once a week with other good treatment until he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 And if you see the patient being cauterized, making several points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cauterization softens the brain equally; and then place moist cotton soaked in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	 of the pain of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When pain first comes to the eyes by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something that cleanses the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat several times in a bath while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 Then instruct the patient to shave his head, and cauterize in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of pain is in both eyes together, or one if it is in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skin during the entire cautery, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against too much blood flow, and if you see too much blood coming out, then compress with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.
dou cors des larmes	 of the body tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 When the tears from the eyes are long-standing and habitual and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then he makes the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of this work on the eyes: I make a cautery in the middle of the forehead, and II cauteries on each temple, and II cauteries on the bridge of the nose below the two bones; and if there is further need, then he cauterizes wisely on top of the eyelid with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 from the body's tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you treat him according to what we have said in the section and it does not help at all, then give the patient three nights of cupped bloodletting; afterwards cleanse his head and make a cautery in the middle of the forehead; and make two cauteries of the type called "clavilis" on each eyelid, a little below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the membrane of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 which has this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you see it, make two cauteries on the two temples as long as the temples are; and do not leave your hand until a third of the membrane is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes turn towards the inside and prick the eye, and then one makes cauteries in two ways: that is to say, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards make on the skin of the eyes a figure that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then put moistened cotton with egg white and musk oil on the eye, then heat the cautery whose shape is this:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards cauterize over the figure that you have drawn little by little many times, so that the hair is burned in that place; and the sign of the healthiness of the work is that you see the skin retracted, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then put moistened cotton with butter until the burn is healed; afterwards continue the care of ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if after that the hairs come back, and the skin is softened, then begin the cautery again in the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are lacking, then cauterize until the skin returns to its natural place, is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one .З., and grind them well together; and do it hastily, so that it does not cool; then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes; and if the disease is in only one eye, then one should work in one, and if in both alike; and place moistened cotton under the eye with egg white; and let the patient's eye be in your health and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press one end and the egg white every time the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for they feel the burning as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the inflammation has passed, lift the bandage from its place, and inspect if you see the skin raised as if it were raised by constriction of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has not worked, until your workings are equal and your eyes focused; then place cotton soaked in butter on it until the burned heart falls off, afterwards cure the place of the inflammation which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to protect yourself well during your work with great care that none of the medicine enters the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the medicine again on that spot which has been softened by the paper, just as you did before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and in smallness, and according to this will be your constraints; and do not answer the straight path for him who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you cure fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you make a cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Command the patient to place his head in your hand; and let the assistant hold his head between your hands so that it does not move or lower his head; then put moistened cotton wool in vinegar or juice of parsley on the eye; afterwards, heat the cautery which is thus: and it is shaved on the head like the feather of a goose, along with which is the cautery; if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent; but nevertheless, this one which is shaved is worthier for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the putrefaction, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and draw forth the pus; afterwards, place a very hot cautery strongly, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the neck above the eye, so that your hand does not move foolishly; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you approach the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then start the cautery again once more, and another if necessary, and let it be for III days; after which apply a piece of cotton moistened in butter, and perform the drying ointment cure until it is healed, and if XL days pass without healing, then apply a corrosive medicine so that the bone may be exposed; and act accordingly as it would come in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a manner of cautery for fistula, which some of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Cut into the fistula and open the place; afterwards put into the opening one subtle piece of wool of this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 And they do so in the amount of one .З. of lead; and hold your hand firmly on the cautery, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead runs into his eye; and it is necessary to place a dampened cotton cloth soaked in egg whites or vinegar over the patient's eye: the lead thus heals the fistula, and the healthy area by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then it is necessary to administer a perforation at the nose, and return the fistula to the body of the nose according to what is appropriate in its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Mouth
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these cracks as we have said in the previous sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery knife like this:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it immediately into the cracks until it reaches the bottom; then treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the gum, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and it festers and rots and becomes inflamed and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in previous sections, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; then burn or perforate the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the fire reaches to the bottom of it, and to the surrounding area; and do this once or twice, then treat as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the corrupt bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure them with medicines and it does not work, then place the patient's head in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery in such a way that you put a reed on the tooth; and quickly put hot cautery inside, and hold your hand steady so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards let the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and then spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the moving tooth is confirmed, and the softened gum is restricted, and the corrupt moisture is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	 of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When toothache comes from cold, whether there is cold or snow, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: cautery with butter and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 Cautery with butter is such that you take butter from a cow and put it on the tip of an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a needle, and dip it in boiled butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth and hold it until it cools down; and do this often until its power reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see it moistening wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it so that the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a rod of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, which will be formed later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be relieved that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter before this cautery, and then rinses vigorously; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery of whatever part you wish, according to what you are able; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	 Of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When scrofula are of cold and moist phlegm, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as indicated below, and have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other part of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it for three days; then place moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; after that, treat the area with onions and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 Li: The (or "the")
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 Quant: When (or "when")
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Quant les chenals dou pormon sont plains de chole, adonques covient que tu te garde que tu ne fai mie cautere a la racine de la gorge, mes fai I autre cautere as espanoles dou chief ou il covient.
de la toust	 Quant li chenals du pormon est plains de sanc, adonques covient que tu te garde que tu ne feis mie cautere a la racine de la gorge, mes fai I autre cautere as espanoles dou chief ou il covient.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 Quant tous les chenals du pormon sont plains de flegme, adonques covient que tu te garde que tu ne feis mie cautere a la racine de la gorge, mes fai I autre cautere as espanoles dou chief ou il covient.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see it, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery which is called "point" from which the form comes before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or thereabout.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the place according to what was said before, and let the cautery be at three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because the cauteries are lighter, therefore you make them three times in succession.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 After the patient has been anointed on his back and sides; then lift the heart which is inside the tickling of your left hand's fingers; and if the joint is dislocated inwards, heat the cautery that has two branches like this.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the side, and three more cauteries will follow; this cautery is made with the three-branched cautery, which is why the figure of the cautery consists of seven branches; and the branches are according to the subtlety of a tent, and that is the form of the three-branched cautery.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one branch, which is why there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After place the cautery on, crush with salt; after that make the patient rest, and let the limb not be moved for a long time until it is well-settled.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the shoulder, or with many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture that they pull it to its complexion, and there are many catarrhs for him, and according to the accustomed manners of cures, if he does not profit at all, then it is necessary that the patient be turned over on his back, and stretch out his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 And for this, he makes three cauterizations: one under the cup of the foot through the quantity of a finger, throughout the entire cautery is clavicle, and two cauterizations on the two sides so that the shape of the cauterizations forms three angles, and there is such space between them when they emit pus that they are not joined together; and let the cauterizations be so deep that they reach the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjoining:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and whoever is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you wish to increase; then cauterize the entire cautery which is called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the previous treatment, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and great windiness, so that it is very much displaced from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him at all, then it is necessary for the patient to be cauterized on his liver; and there should be a sign of three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this amount on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come; and there should be a space between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and the cauteries should be long in the body, and do not press too hard with your hand over the entire cautery; and let only half the head be burned, and let the patient lie on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if it pleases you, cauterize these cauteries of the cuticle, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and let it not reach the boil, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient does not feel pain too severely; and if it is in the membrane, they feel insane pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then, when this cure should be performed by the doctors, it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and then sign the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a grape, as here is its form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And you should cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burned, and it comes to the spleen, so that the entire tumor is destroyed; after the cure according to the cure of the swellings, until he is healed; and it is not necessary for this cautery to be used by anyone but one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whom few of these diseases have run their course.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that one should make for pleurisy cauteries of the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and grasp it with fire, and cauterize I cautery between the sternum and the neck, and II small cauteries a little below in the part that is under the beard; and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, slanting behind a little; and I cautery in the middle of the chest, and I another on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II on the sides of the chest opposite the cautery which is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancients say that a man uses fire cautery similar to a razor, and heats it and places it between the ribs, until it reaches that abscess; and then the pain ceases, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula may develop which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 from the bladder
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you treat the disease of the bladder according to what we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three methods of fire cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 One of the methods is that you make three cauteries, or four, in a line according to the length of the bladder, similar to the liver cautery which we have spoken of before; and do not press your hand onto the entire cautery, and let the patient lie on his back. Another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the skin which is near the bladder, towards the left side of the patient's ribs, and the lifting should be according to the ribs, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
