And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it opens the heart, and then do another part in the middle slit to the other side; and then draw blood equally, and press the place for the blood drawn; then put a tent of old cotton into each slit, and put wet cloths on top with wine, oil, and vinegar, and make sure no abscess comes there; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and apply a large quantity of boiled water, then a basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 Of the pain of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When cataracts come to someone suddenly, and you see the eyes dim and small, and vision is weakened, and the eyelids are burnt; and hair falls out, and there is sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those substances and that cataract do not come from one vein, but from many. And the treatment for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And so you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one from the hairline.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the cut go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples’ nerves that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton and linen between the two lips of the incision; then bind over it cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with drying substances that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 En such manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, make a poultice from them; and apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 of the blockage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grain, an animal, a mineral stone or something similar like iron; or seed, such as barley, beans, peas; or a fluid thing, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear that is not compatible with it and does not grow in the ear, such as a stone or any other kind of thing, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, drop a little bit of violet oil or sesame oil into it, then apply extraction; and make him sneeze by blowing in his face, and block his nostrils when he is about to sneeze, and wrap around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Much of the time fever occurs with this treatment; and if it does not occur, then use fine forceps for extraction, which is the form here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If the fever comes with forceps, it is good; if not, then use a fine extraction hook of small thickness; and if it does not come with that, make a tube of brass and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole strongly, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube; then pull fever strongly, for much of the time fever comes in this way as we have said; and if the fever does not come in such a manner, then take glue as birds take, and put it into some instrument which is suitable to do this, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and pull fever.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et si elle ne saut pas de toutes ces choses que nous avons dites, hâte-toi de fendre l'oreille avant qu'un abcès ou une crampe n'y vienne. La manière de la fendre est ainsi : fais d'abord saigner le malade par la céphalique, et tire du sang selon la mesure de sa vertu ; puis fais asseoir le malade entre tes mains et tourne l'oreille vers le haut. Fais une petite fendre à la racine de l'oreille dans la graisse ou le lieu voisin ; que la fente soit comme un croissant, jusqu'à ce que tu atteignes la pierre, puis retire-la selon ton pouvoir et suce hâtivement à ta bouche ; et fais la cure jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Et si c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si administrez extraction;
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then perform a subtle and thin incision on the grain according to this form:
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with subtle tweezers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to first sneeze by inhaling condiments, and then clean the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it leaps out through the sky, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If not through the sky, then take many small and light pebbles according to the length of your thumb, heat them a little in the fire; and put one into the patient's ear where it hurts, and let him jump on his feet on the other side, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this from stone to stone until all the water comes out, and so it jumps out completely; and if you see, take a reed, put one end into the ear, and hold the other end in the fire until the nearest part of the reed burns; then repeat with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said in the case of stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 In the extraction of the beast, if it is small in size, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use the extraction of pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if any worms appear, extract them with fine pincers; and if they do not appear, take the hair of which this is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And pour the most subtle liquid into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then draw out all the wax; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey in coming out, then plug around the wax with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out strongly as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and thus distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, which is shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And whether of silver or bronze, place under a small opening, and above to drip; and for pressing during the distillation, use a well-made bronze tool for this purpose; and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip securely; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you have in the funnel, and let the funnel be in the ear; then put inside the scraper all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed over the fire before being distilled in the ear; and ensure that it is not too cold, for then the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear piercing
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to piercing of a wound, or of flesh growing inside the ear, and this piercing sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is not enough of an opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Therefore, if it goes deep and cannot be seen, it is of grave significance in many ways, and in that which can be seen, you must place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the hair appearing, then perform this operation with whatever tool forms this.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind entirely, so that it does not wound the ear; if the incision is from flesh born or from the body of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and cut gently, until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the incision goes deep into the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the incision which causes the patient pain to touch, puncture lightly and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and soak it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this every day until the wound is healed: take a tent and soak it in rose water, then sprinkle powdered vitriol on it. And if you see the ear swell, you must remove the tent and replace it with another tent soaked in wax made of rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is gone; then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if blood comes out, take a sponge and soak it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding, which are discussed in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	 from the flesh of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This althelul that comes from the eyes of birds when they are wet and dry, you must pull them out with tweezers and pinchers, then scrape off a piece of its root with a spatula; then place powdered vitriol on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 Et se sans en decort, then scrape off the skin, and cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and after the incision, it is better to move; and often they return, when some root remains; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	 of gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times there come to the eyes certain things that resemble gravel in shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "grandine," and it is a thick gathering of moisture above and below the eye; the treatment is such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, which is an easy thing to know; then make an incision wide enough, then scrape each part lightly, then grasp it with forceps, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it without piercing the skin a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, join it with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment restores it quickly and regenerates flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And if the hail descends into the ear towards the upper part, invert the skin and stretch the hail with tweezers; and cover it and press from both sides; and if the skin is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hail is covered, lift the eye of salt water, and treat the place with that which regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Of the exanthema is a fat that is secreted into the tissues of the eyelids, and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly afflicts their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the sunlight because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they always lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moistened by the exanthema that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press your fingers against it, you feel the exanthema between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the manner of this procedure is that the patient puts his head in your hands; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained by exanthema from each part, then place it on him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exanthema is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit wide enough, but not larger than the incision made for venesection; and pierce the skin through to the exanthema; and in many cases it comes out from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Pull out then all in one piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is scattered; and beware not to approach the cleft, lest you come all the way to the little eye, that you may not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the skin does not open at the beginning of the cleft, then gently widen the cleft slightly until it opens; then pull as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure him until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there comes a hot abscess in the place, then cure it with soothing poultices until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When in the eyes hairs grow that are different from the natural ones, and they are irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as tearing and softening of the eyes and cataracts, to the point of causing blindness; and the cure is done in four ways: either by cautery with fire, or by medical treatment according to what was said before in the chapter on cautery, and this can be done either by incision and suturing or by caustics, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your hands, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, then push a needle with all its thread on top; and let this be at the margin of the paper where the hairs are born near these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision in the part below the paper, below the close-set hairs, cutting all the way from the great tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the paper; then sign above the paper a figure like a myrtle leaf, and yet it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount that you wish to raise the paper which is devised for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if one has need to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the great larmier until small; and let one of the clefts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the ointment into one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all; then gather the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluity of the threads stick on the two sorcerers with any gluey thing if you want to do this; and if not, then have no concern about it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three days or four; then heal the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the paper heals by the closing of the wound and its gathering, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you cut the paper in a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have said, with three unwrapped ointments according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Then cut that which surmounts the small forces equally according to the form that is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and push it into the figure; and push another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have sewn, as we have said, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with wax and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair on the skin is turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one place and another is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 The cure of the hairs is as follows: you must turn the paper and the opening inside as I have said, then make two hairs by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; and cut both ends of both parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other finely on what exceeds from the paper of the eye, and strongly tighten the two hairs in the two parts; and leave it this way for some days, and the skin that is tightly pulled will die and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it is delayed, then cut with a strong force, then cure it until it heals; and when the wound is healed and the paper is removed, the hairs will no longer grow. And this is the form of the two hairs that you will make according to this figure and in this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 The work is such that you should take a fine needle, and insert a soft and fine silk thread into it; then bring the heads together and knot them both finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the shaft another fine silk thread briefly, and knot the ends of the thread; then have the patient put his head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work, then insert the needle into the entire shaft at the root of the hair close to it, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the top of the shaft, and insert that hair into the shaft, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out completely from the shaft in the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the arrow is removed and the hair does not come out with it, then you will draw the arrow from below along all the thread that you have ordered there, until the arrow comes out through the hole above and you see it with your eye; then you will remove the arrow and the thread, and close the eye and let it remain closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh heals; and if the hair is small, then accompany it with one long natural hair, and lift it with that which you leave, until it becomes elongated and then you remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the infection of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or infection comes to the eye, there are two types of it: one is natural and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly by a wound, or by cutting, or by cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of working on it is that you split open this suture, and separate its lips, and put inside linen tents, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not necessary to use in its cure things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and moisten it with water or honey and flax seeds boiled, and fat of the hyena melted in some of the oils, and wrap it in a tent, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your care is that you take care lest it heals not according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is not outside of addressing this illness, lest it return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from a wound and a tear and a cautery and similar things; and the way of working in it is that you take a needle, on which there are two threads, and the tip in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left corner to the right, so that the thread comes into two corners of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut with one wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the figure of the stone returns as it should be, it is good; if not, then take a rasp and place it in the groove, and turn the stone, and make two grooves on either side inside the stone; and let the heads of the two grooves be at the two corners of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle such that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which is called "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the sharpness of its sides below, from what follows the stone, then bring together the two divided parts, and sew them with a woolen thread; then follow the cure as we have said of softening medicines, and compresses, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And if the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, you must make a clean cut under the hairs of the skin, according to what was said before; then remove between the two lips of a tent as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine with all his power to bring back the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 then sew the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When this sewing happens to many people in such a way that the skin on top is sewn with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is necessary then that you put the point of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and stretch with tweezers until you cut what is close to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or cutting, so that the patient cannot tolerate being cut by the too sharp spatula in the eye; and your incision, from which you remove that gathering, should be light, so that the skin returns according to its natural form; and all that gathering is healed, and sometimes there is salt water in the eye, and a lift of fresh water and coloring; then put between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and place on the eye wet wool in abundance of egg; and after three days use coloring and healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the fingernail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 You should know that the nail is in two ways: one is like a hard nerve, and another which is not like a nerve, but is like frozen white moisture; when you touch it with iron and try to grasp it with pincers, no one can. And both resemble each other starting from the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then opens his eyes. And raise the eyelid with your hand, then curl the nail with pincers of small double-pointed needles, and place them on top; then take a needle, and insert one horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and a strong thread. And slightly bend the point of the needle and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and place it on top, and scrape all the way along the side of the nail that follows the small vein and the silk to the hair, up to the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with all the subtle spatula and fine forceps, and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that the body does not produce tears through the incision; and sometimes the nails are placed only on the eyelid and the thread, as we have said; then scrape all the soft tissue of which there is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And ensure that the spittle does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the anus is not pierced; and after the incision cast into the eye a little of burnt silk, and made from lead, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not fleshy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, this appearance of a nail is often treated with medicines; and it emerges as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, work the eye of the patient, and take a little spittle in a light way according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 And cut the nail above subtly, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then drip from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of lead and red collyrium powdered and mixed, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is against you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of the flesh of the lacrimal sac comes into the eye by great harm, then suspend it to the eyelid, and cut off a part of it but not all, so that no watery body comes into it; then drip into the eye red collyrium which is made from lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 of the flesh that grows upon the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 of some men’s eyes grows sometimes red flesh, which covers the eyelid and extends onto the whites of the eye, turning them outward, resembling a rose on a baluster; and the procedure is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then you open the eyes, and cut all that flesh with scissors suitable for this purpose, and hold it firmly; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the root until the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the nail and in small forces from which one removes the scab, as the figure following this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with warm egg white mixed with vinegar, so that it forms a hot poultice on the eye; and if anything remains and the pus overcomes you, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with substances that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do this whenever flesh grows in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 But nevertheless, you must choose the cure for each weak eye in accordance with nature; and by accident, in ironwork; and do not venture your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is capable of enduring such work.
des voines des eulz	 from the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 They are red veins that cover the eye and obstruct vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, the first thing to consider is whether the eye, in which this vein is found, is sound and free from any other illness except for the vein; then deal with the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, then lift those veins with a fine thread according to his skill, and let the thread be double and subtle according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And there are two bones by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 and when the forces of those veins are subtly cooled, and wipe away the blood hour by hour until you see those strong veins recede from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very ardent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains from the black.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you do not have the power to cool all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and the hot abscess is assured, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 The doctor calls it an "ardent" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a tumor in it that you should cut over the abscess, where it must die, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take out all the instrument that is in this form; and it is called an "aspre" head, and let it be made of iron with a sharp point, and let it be shaped like a file as shown in the present figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And place it on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then apply drying medicines to the place.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed, and flesh grows over it, and the body of the bowel is sealed, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed, and no evil incident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other device than to redirect the fistula towards the neck according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a foret according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it on the bone near the edge, and remove your hand from the eye by a fistful, then turn the entire foret until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand to his neck; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have shown you, and when the flesh grows and the wound hardens, the matter goes to the neck; thus it is a lighter burden for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is completely open and there is no hindrance to vision or reduction in sight, then you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply cupping without piercing to draw out, then place on the eye a plaster made of alum and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then hold the eye, and bandage over with cloths and linen; and the manner of the linen is such that you take linen soft enough, and fold each in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind tightly with a strong bandage, and reapply the cupping without piercing; then remove the cupping and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the plaster softens, then you must bind it very tightly; then remove the plaster after the day and night, and if you see the eye heal, that is good; if not, then recommence the plaster and the linen and the plaster and the cupping until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 Dou du rompement of toile ou veue
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When disruption occurs in the uvea, it opens, and exudes from the tissues like a grain of resin, which is frightening to see; then if you wish to close it, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the affected part up to its top, then insert another needle where there is a double filament in the tear duct; and make it pierce through, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut off the place of the double filament and tie around one part of the uvea, securing it well, then withdraw the needle and apply a moist linen cloth abundantly with egg yolk on the eye; leave it until the threads join with the uvea, then treat the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by the uvea from all around in a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eye has great swelling, perforate it with a fine spatula that reaches to the bottom of the eye, and let the purulent moisture flow out and descend from the eye, and enter in quickly; then extract until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the white of the eye which is collected in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a well-prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it until you see the white come above your eyes; then let it be inserted, and do not let it descend and be obscured the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the white is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the patient sits between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make an incision on the corneal cloth in the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal cloth and the cornea, until the bubble comes out; and when it has come out, drip hot water mixed with honey into the eye, or hot fenugreek water boiled with honey, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 From the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have here similarities to the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; thus we proceed according to healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, out of the light of the sun; and he ties the sound eye and squeezes it very hard; then put the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eye is left, or to your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a ray on that whiteness of the eye at the minor lacrimal part, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the void place; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be to the depth of the measure of the space that is from the prunelle up to the end of the pupil; and this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneal cloth, and then put the instrument until it reaches the place where the water is, then press under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If water comes now, let the patient see it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again by the second path, place the fire with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently draw the almagda while turning your hand little by little; then put in some clean water, and lift out of that eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place on the eye cotton or wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 Yes, and we who are of our time, place it on top like breadcrumbs with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And so pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle; then put almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed, on which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be bound according to his condition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you lift him up, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 Et puis isse de la maison poc a poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 Et puis isse de la maison poc a poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 Et puis isse de la maison poc a poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And let the head of them be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	 on the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes hairs grow on the nose, which are different and some resemble many-legged scorpions; and there are such that have hair of fiery red color, and some have soft hair of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Therefore, in that hair which is soft and not hooked, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and throw the onion to those hairs, and pull them out; then cut off what you can hold with a subtle pointed spatula from one side, until you know that all the hair has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if there remains any matter that cannot be covered, then open it all up with subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it surmounts you or if an abscess forms, then aid it as is necessary; and if it is malignant apostemes, then hasten and cauterize until the flesh is charred and all the pus is removed, then cast into fresh water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 And if the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is a bone spur in the upper bone, which prevents the instrument from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen about a hand’s width thick, and have it tied by my hands, and let there be between each knot a distance of one finger or less; and let the patient place the end of the thread in his nose as strongly as he can, and pull until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and often children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know each in turn as I do with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this so that you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then remove the thread, wipe off the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead plug in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if dry medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, into which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And let it be of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and the tube likewise; and if you wish, make a closed plug, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 Of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 Frequently a disease called "telul" appears on the tip of the nose and grows large so that it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason you should cut it off at the beginning, and remove all force, then apply the cautery or burning medicine in place; and if one delays cutting until it is large, beware if it is hard, with a purple color, with poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an ulcer, because when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the ulcer is of soft texture, not of purple color, and you see that one can completely cut it off, let the patient fast and cut without fear, and treat the place with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when healing continues to come into one of these cartilage works, it benefits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If this happens to anyone, first consider if the wound is fresh and full of blood; then join the two lips with one stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from both sides, then you must cauterize all the parts of their heart until they are healed, then join the two lips with one stitch, and hold it, and put on powder of dragon's blood and ground incense; and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of sewing is such that you bring together the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have taught you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In many people there occurs within the lips a hard abscess, resembling grains of millet, smaller and larger; then you must turn back the lips and cut above each knot, and take it with pincers and chop it in every part; then fill the place after the incision with vitriol powdered until the wound is cauterized; and then apply alum and treat the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 From the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Often there appears on the gums a piece of flesh that the ancients call "albulus"; then you must grasp it with tongs and cut it at its root, allowing the abscess or blood to drain; then apply powdered vitriol or other restraining and drying powders to the spot; and if this flesh returns after cutting, as often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: then it will not return after cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 from sores
