Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes there are scabs gathered at the roots of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; sometimes the teeth become black and yellow and green, to the point where corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid; then you must make the patient sit in your lap, with their head resting on your chest, and remove the teeth or scabs until nothing remains; and do the same for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned away; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments for removal, according to what the work demands, because the files used for removing from outside the teeth have different shapes than those used for removing between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you cure the tooth of its pain, you delay pulling it as long as possible, for this should not be done; for it is a very high substance until such time as one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull out [the tooth], it is necessary that you be certain about the tooth hurting.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth and pulls out the good tooth; however, the pain does not depart because of this, until the evil string is removed. For we have already seen this happen to these lords; and when you are well certain about the hurting tooth, it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth on all sides with a very hot spatula to protect the gum from every side; then move [the tooth] with your fingers or subtle tongs little by little at first and bit by bit until it is well loosened. Then firmly grasp the tongs, and let the patient's knee be between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, then you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and delicately grip it with pliers so that it does not break when gripping; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be well aware that you do not break it, and a part remains, and the patient returns with greater pain than before due to the root's evil.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act as the ignorant doctors do, who sometimes break the jaw due to their haste and boldness, and do not bring what we have mentioned; but they sometimes cause a great disease due to the roots that remain or the broken jaw, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine, vinegar, or salt; and if blood flows there, which often happens, then fill the area with burnt vitriol; and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 The forms of the instruments, with which one removes teeth first, should be long and thick, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And let them be of thick material so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold well.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after pulling, then you must place on the spot cotton soaked in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the place is softened, then put in the pincers which are called "algefri", with which the tooth seems like a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, then you must uncover the flesh completely around the root, and put there the instrument called "althali," which is to say tweezers, of which here is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out this way, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one helps oneself with this instrument that has two pincers, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other tools that are before in the manner of teeth, and of this tool that resembles large pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And this instrument should be such that it cannot break; and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and similarly for other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master subtly finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness shows him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity of forms. And if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, where it could, then he seeks the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with suitable medicines. And if there is rot in the bone and it is small, then use this instrument for all of it:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 When the teeth appear not according to nature's body, and the shape is ugly, especially in maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is growing after the other teeth, and it is not in its right place, and cannot be pulled or filed: then extract it; and if it is crooked with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and it is similar to a small beak, and let it be of sharp iron at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the clamp little by little each day because of the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is prominent enough to be filed, file it with a file like this shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 And it is also like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little each day lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out; then level it at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must file the roughness until it is equal, so that it no longer cuts the tongue or corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	 When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front tooth loosens, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot eat what they want without it falling out, and you have treated it with restricting medicines, but to no avail; then you must restrain it with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but the gold never moves; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the knot between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you wisely reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then restart the wrapping from the beginning, and subtly and wisely tighten your hand so that it does not move; and let the tie be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then cut the heads of the wire with pliers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and position it so that it does not hurt the tongue; then let it stay like this for as long as possible, and if it becomes loose or the wire breaks, then hold it in place with another wire; thus it will remain and serve its purpose for all time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth, and two canines, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and no one should interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes a form of a cow’s bone tooth, and places it where the defect is, and holds it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper to fasten the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Another time this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, as one is born thus; or by accident of a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from a sudden wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament; and beware that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you have done it, lift the place with rose water and alum, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen cloth; and let the patient lick every night, so that the place cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if blood continues to flow, place a vitriol plaster on the spot; and if it overcomes the flesh, cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this; then treat with another treatment until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see that the flesh is of a dark or black color and hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it tends towards a pustule, and there is moisture, apply onion, and make an incision with a fine spatula, and deliver from one side and the other; and if the flesh overcomes your work, place a vitriol plaster until it is cauterized, then return to your work until you extract everything; then lift the spot with oil and vinegar, and treat with other treatments until healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes there are abscesses in the throat called «godath», and they are properly called the two amygdales. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, take care: if it is hard abscess of small sense and of gray color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron for the flow of blood; but leave it until it becomes ripe, and then you will divide it, or it would burst on its own; and if it turns white again, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look to see if the abscess is hot and soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his eyes be in your shadow, and he works his mouth and takes the instrument between his hands, and presses the tongue beneath it all the way to the end; and let it be of silver or fine brass, like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 When you have pressed the tongue to the end of this instrument and you see the abscess, take the needle and insert it into the almond, and draw it strongly above as much as you can; and draw some cloths with it, then cut off with the instrument, which has the form of a forceps; however, the ends are curved, one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 Et si tu n'as pas cet instrument sous la main, alors coupe avec des tenailles, voici comment il faut faire :
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 Et si tu n'as pas cet instrument sous la main, alors coupe avec des tenailles, voici comment il faut faire : soit tranchant d’une part, et de l’autre part non ; et quand tu as coupé l’une des amygdales, alors coupe l’autre de la même manière. Ensuite, fais une incision et rince la bouche du patient avec de l'eau chaude et de l'eau de vie, et si du sang coule, alors rince la bouche du patient avec de l'eau dans laquelle ont été cuites des écorces de grenades ou des feuilles de myrte, jusqu’à ce que le sang soit coagulé ; puis soigne la blessure jusqu’à ce qu’elle guérisse. Parfois, d'autres abcès apparaissent dans la gorge à côté des deux amygdales, alors coupe-les de la même manière que les deux amygdales également.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two eyes through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened immediately and placed one needle into one opening, then drew it out, and from it issued a great portion of pus; then I did the same in the other opening of the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after which I placed the needle into these abscesses and drained some of it, but only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop trimming that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew back immediately and filled the place I had emptied, until it became very large; then I cauterized it inside the throat: so it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what became of her after me.
de l’uve	 of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below and thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that this abscess is quieted, and it is subtle, then you must cauterize it; and that which is round and not long; and it is red or purple or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned earlier; then insert the onion into the eye, and draw it down, and cauterize it with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you must not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the II almonds, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, then you must use ingenuity in order to calm their fear before cauterizing.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cautery is sharp and acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And it is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses their tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and pierce with a sharp, lively awl, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the end of this instrument, which looks like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And have in the head a little hair where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat, and wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eye, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see it darkened and the irritations of the medicine are soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four days or five. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This remedy is more effective than cutting or cauterizing; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or some of them in a pot, and put ash in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and within the pot there should be an instrument shaped in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or copper, and let one of the heads be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, as long as the eye is affected; after that, repeat it often until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a kettle and put inside it the shell of an egg, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and this is a good cure together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Many times there is a bone or a fish spine stuck in the throat, or something else; therefore, you must extract what you can see, and press the tongue to the instrument, so that you see the object move; and what does not open and remains in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the hard object will come out with the vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread. And tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will hook onto it, and then you will pull it out. And if it does not come out with what we have said, then take an instrument made of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be bent at the tip so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and have the tip raised high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest the tongue or the vein come; do not push in the bone; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is hard; so they push downward, where they draw strongly all the instrument equally, until it is drawn out.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes blood is treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by medicinal treatment; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, after you have pressed the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see blood, then draw it out with the smallest hook, or with subtle tweezers that are suited for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a hollow reed and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the reed's opening, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient is thirsty all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the patient's mouth, and pour it in without choking, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have mentioned for eye fumigation; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the method of fumigation is such that you take a pot with clear-sighted charcoal, and the lid be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and have the patient put the end of the cane in their mouth, and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes to the phlegm; and the phlegm will now fall out, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient should bear thirst, and eat salty things and such, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for her to come out through this procedure.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood, it is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pincers for entering the throat; and let it resemble the beak of a bird of prey, and it should have the roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many types of abscesses, as remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways, one is similar to its own appearance, and the other because it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 car the abscess of the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess in the fleshy part is different from that which comes to the joints, and each must be judged in its work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And so there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is ripe according to its development; and there are those which must be pierced when they become hardened, and do not ripen according to their development, such as abscesses near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 Because when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it be until it is rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted, which causes constriction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; when it is near the anus, it should be perforated as soon as it is ripe; and one should not perforate a newly formed abscess before digestion is complete, except for that which is near the anus, lest it becomes worse and deeper, and causes a fistula; and it cannot heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And you should know the time for perforating an abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the fever subsides, and the redness and swelling decrease, and there is a change in the appearance of the abscess head, and other signs; and you should make the incision where the abscess is most dependent, and where it has opened up; and let the incision be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no folding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is healed with complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you open it before that, the body will be longer filled with its poison, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is any abscess that needs to be opened according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where you need to remove the core, and cover; when it is fully developed like linen, and it is dead, it is necessary to do as with buboes: and if there are those that are divided into three angles, and if there are those from which one cuts like a myrtle leaf, as abscesses of the anus; and if there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 That which has no head, such as a superficial abscess, it must be pierced completely. And when the abscess is large and has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all of the pus in that hour, but only some; then pack the abscess with wool until the next day, then draw out something again; do this many times from great to small, until all the pus is released. Similarly if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit jumps sometimes with the exit of the pus, which may cause the patient to die, and you will not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, and when you have perceived your abscess, then wash the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must insert a bandage into each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess and removed a piece of skin, then you must fill it with old cotton or lint without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold and easy water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, then bring governance and care, and the powders that I have said in less quantity in this book, and if it is in winter and the place of the abscess is very nervous, then you must place on tents and cloths moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer and the place is fleshy, then you must place on cloths moistened with water and oil, or wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then uncover the abscess and dry and treat it, as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where the head has small abscesses, and they are similar to us in that they are in clusters, like the bristles of a hedgehog, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are fatty ones and such that have moisture like pustules; and there are such that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not make a mistake.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the cutting is such that you should try every instrument that is called an "incision tool," from which the form comes hereafter, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 If it contains moisture, then open it from above the long [bone].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left there; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and this will cure those who have been affected by the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that nothing remains of the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds the eye (or vision), then cut according to this form, along the length; and throw in your onions, and skin it from all sides, and put all your care into drawing out the force from beneath where it lies; and if the surgeon does something contrary, then do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do likewise for the abscess if it is pious (or purulent), and in cutting and caring as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut over the purulent and moist abscess, for it is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if there are any of these abscesses that have no moisture at the top, like those abscesses that I cut at the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one were to strike against it, one would cause as much injury as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming to the head, except those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, so that the pus may exit; and treat it as needed.
des scrophules	 of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess occurs on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes it comes to other parts of the body, and they are very numerous, and they are interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically inside its own shell, like the nut and the head abscess, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, and it is similar in color to the body, and soft from all sides and not harsh on the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and not deep; then you must cut it from above, and scrape from each side, and extend the two lips of the heart to the corners, if you need it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel be neither too sharp nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not move too far forward, lest you cut something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that staunch blood, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and begins to putrefy.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then check with your finger if there remain any small scrofula, and cut and clean them away.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut all the scrofula, then it is necessary that you join the two lips of the wound, and sew them together now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 it is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and pull strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae that have superfluity, pierce there where it appears dark; and pierce in the same way as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then introduce bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with enchanting flesh ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	 of scurvy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is written according to their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have scurvy, it is necessary to remove the cleft of the throat called "epiglottis"; and do not use this method because all the veins and the mouth of the patient are hot due to abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cut off the epiglottis to avoid death from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must make the incision below three or four small rings, between two rings or by the size of the tracheal incision, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no bone, and the vessels are long. )))
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the neck, then split the heart until it reaches the throat; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, then cut the sinew, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the throat which jumps forth through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the time has passed in which strangulation is feared, join the two lips of the heart's wound, and sew it all alone without a bandage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis said that one should not do this until the throat is completely filled, and the patient is judged to be dead, and there is a lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then the epiglottis is cut so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus he is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the harm of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young lady took a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the hollows of the larynx; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I discovered the wound, and found that blood had come out of it, although it had not struck a vein or artery other than the throat, and the wind was coming out strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed the wound, and treated it until it healed; and no harm came to the damsel except that she was hoarse of voice, and afterwards returned to her normal state; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a great abscess in the color of jet, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural, and accidental; in the natural kind there is no fever.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is according to two manners, of which one resembles grass on us, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it is not right to work with fire except in the small one, and prove and search throughout the intromission: if you find it as we do with grass, and it does not hurt any vein, then cut it off, as we cut the nose, and draw all its cover, if there is any; and seek well early, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many manners are of us, of which I will say all the resemblances; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between grass and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 I say that the issue occurs along with fever and heat until the swelling passes and the suppuration is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With the knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own sac and matches the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and grows large; and they are of two kinds, either thick or thin, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, that you try and probe first with all the instruments which are called "introducers," according to what their shape will be in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of the examination of abscesses is that you take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the heart, according to the size of the abscess; then remove the probe, and be careful not to let it jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If the flowing moisture stops, and if it has color, then puncture it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the probe no more moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, so then puncture it crosswise, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it from each side, and watch the cloth where it lies to draw it out cleanly with the thread; and if you cannot draw it out cleanly, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 Car if anything remains there, the nose will return many times; and if a little remains and the flesh is inflamed, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and bind the wound, and apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and perform other treatments until it heals; and if the nose is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it as one would with gangrenous flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 and if the vein is pulsating against you or otherwise, then hurry and fill the place with broiled vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound putrefies, and the blood boil ceases; then return to the copper that remains of the nose.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the instruments used for insertion, and there are three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to surround the fistula abscesses; and they are like the needles used to sew sorceries, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow in color are worth more, and they are more proven for dipping in black lead to surround the fistula abscesses; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of onions are very diverse, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; there are also onions that have two curves in three different ways; and there are onions that have three curves, also in three different ways; and there are onions that have two curves, and single-curved onions, all in three different ways; and all these are necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these instruments are sharpened, and among them are those that cut only from one side, with which we peel the noses, lest we cut the vein or nerve; and these instruments include the retractors called handles, so that the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses. They come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places. Sometimes a smaller instrument is made, resembling the sheaths of arrows, like this, with which we staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 and it is sometimes placed at the site that heals quickly of veins, and of arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them must follow this form according to these lines from .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine containing meat, then join the two lips of the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as happens to women, then make two cuts above on either side, through two similar slits; so that one may adhere to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to this line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powder, and whatever is necessary for the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in caustic ointment; and leave it until it has consumed the remainder and the fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 from the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 This abscess that comes from under the armpits is like hard scrofula with ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is like scrofula, cut it as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound releases pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of the cutting/tearing of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is cut and the skin above it is stitched, often abscesses form. This also happens with an inflamed vein and abscess; and you can tell if it's due to the artery, because the abscess is long and deep. And when you touch it with your fingers, you feel constriction. And when it's due to the vein, the reason becomes apparent; and it's foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it's under the soles of the feet, in the groins, in the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment with iron, and whoever has it in their head should also avoid it, and for one suffering from swelling of an artery, make a long incision in the skin; then work on the incision at the corners, and separate the artery from the skin, until it is exposed; then insert below it a needle and make it go through to the other side, and tighten the artery with two threads in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then stitch up the place between the two threads with an intromitter until the pus comes out that is there, and the abscess will be relieved; then administer treatment like a boil, until the thread falls off; then treat it with ointments appropriate to this, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of the vein, you must take in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle below the place you hold in your hand, and make it go through, and let there be a double thread, so that you draw it out on the other side; then tie up the abscess, as I have said, with the end of one of the two threads to the two ends of the filaments; and if you doubt that the thread will come out too much, insert another needle all along one thread below all the abscess at the first incision, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess skin and leave what is tied up; then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments of bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	 of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Just like abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are cut, or due to too much work, and similar things.
