Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and in the arms, and in all places where there are joints, and these are very severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when it is pressed firmly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not at all in the depth of the flesh, but below the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and those which are in joints should not be cut with iron: lest a contraction may occur; and those which are on the head or forehead, make an opening for the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on an awl, scrape it, then remove and close the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging large abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to them, and it has subtle roots, and a large head; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were always oozing moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six, and the work in the incision is such that you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is pale and moist and of subtle root; thus, cut with a broad spatula, and let the cautery be near the fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For often in cutting there is too much bleeding and if the wound bleeds too much then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain [the patient], and do not stop pulling the linen thread until you cut the joint, and it will come out without difficulty; and if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting itself for the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the ligament which is of dark color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Because it is an encrusted abscess, I will come to the treatment of the chancre hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the swelling is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the swelling comes from a burn or a cut on the body, and it is on the belly and in some of the scrotum, as happens with other rotations, either from blood coming out of veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rotation of the intestine and the exit of the bladder, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and it opens in different ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is even more diverse; and when one presses it with his fingers, it swells up, and then returns, and perhaps becomes hard, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and from great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 Et si c'est par moisteur, c'est chose legiere, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne l'en contrains mie; et si c'est par sanc, si apert par ces signes que l'aposteme est gros et dur, et il est fichie selon une certaine quantite; et si c'est par ventositeit, il est doux au toucher, et l'ouvrage est tel que tu regardes si les apparences sont dues au sang de l'artère, ou de la veine, ou de la ventositeit.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Et li sancs delivre et le mal en va.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Qui veut estraindre les oelz quant il fait son caueterie de feu.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to intestines or bladder, then you must instruct the patient to hold his thigh, and lie straight; then sign all around the abscess; then command him to rest calmly between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with all the pus; then extend half of the abscess above onto the large hook; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the thread be secure; then work the half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, then untie it, and push the intestine out from the belly; and if you find the bladder, then take it with the hook, and cut off the excess; and if the instrument or the vein does something against you, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads through them, and push the two needles through what you have done in a cross that you have punctured; then press the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall by itself; or you cut it when it is subtilized and rotten, then cure it as needed, and heal the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as needed, and close the place.
dou chancre	 of cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division the similarities of cancer, and how one should work with medicines therein, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we say that cancer develops in the flesh, and great care is needed in the cure, and the ancients said that when the cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, such as cancer in the breasts, and in the thigh, and similar places, one should remove it all when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile; then make him fast if he has obvious fullness, then put the patient in a good place to perform the work; then cast your nails on the cancer, and scrape from all sides, and remove from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood run freely, and press well the place with your hand or any object, and if the flow of blood hinders you from incising the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then cure by another method until he is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: this is only in the case of "eclites"; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympanites and hydrops, for it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this resemblance of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not help, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as diarrhea and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is danger; and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient upright in your hands, and the assistant presses the stomach by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the pointed lancet according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 Et soit tranchant de deux parties.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 a point, and yet it should not be so sharp that when inserted, it can reach the intestines and injure them; then observe if the dropsy is towards the intestines: in this case, you must make an incision above the navel three fingers' width to the right of the pubic bone; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side; and if it is due to spleen enlargement, it should be on the right; and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluidities do not run to this weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand along with the entire layer between the skin and the membrane as if peeling, to the quantity of a nail or around it; then pierce the membrane until the layer comes to the expected place, which is the watery place; then draw out the instrument strongly, and insert this instrument whose form I have described:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a silver needle of fine quality, and it is made of lightweight brass or copper; and on the lower part there is one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another side; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribes use to cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 on the top is the air hole, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it rises immediately onto the instrument; empty then half or one-third of it, because if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he falls into a coma, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulse; then draw the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the cork that stops the hole which is on the syphon, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then renew the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to overdo it so that only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and you leave much water in him, then cure him with hot sand or charcoal, and by sweating profusely in a bath and in the sun, and let him drink wine; and cure him with desiccative medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach, on the liver, and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the impediment of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without a hole in the penis, or with a small hole, or one that is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it must be pierced immediately so that he does not have to wait until puberty; the tool must be very fine, like this:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then place in the hole a subtle plug of linden wood, and bind it and hold it thus for III days or IV, and when one wishes to make urine, let the plug be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes out freely does not leave a plug.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 Those whose hole is small should be treated with the linden wood plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those whose hole is not in its place are injured, for some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, preventing them from urinating forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the womb, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies face up on his back, then extend the head of the penis and the foreskin as much as the length of a feather, so that the opening is centered in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding that occurs frequently, and if it happens, stanch it like one who staunches blood, and heal the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 Of the pimples on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these pimples appear on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; therefore you must take them with a fine needle, and cut and clean all of them, then put on moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with ointment of laudanum until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the bath is malignant, with foul color and stench, then you must bring cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have struck it, and if the bath is in part on the stick, and has part within the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the bath that is within; and when it is healed, then treat the one outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat them together, it is not certain that the head of the stick will not be pierced, and there will be blackening and corruption in the stick and in the joint; therefore one must cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and beans, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if the flow of blood continues, bring the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery helps in two conditions together: that is to say, for the flow of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert into the channel of the penis a lead tube, and the patient urinates through it; and when the hair at the head of the penis, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, happens due to wound or abscess, it is then necessary that you scrape it with one curved instrument until the connection is released and the head of the penis is freed on all sides; and if it is a serious matter to discuss this, it is necessary that you scrape with one small spatula some part of the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate between two, and place one fine linen cloth moistened in cold water there, so that it does not swell again.
de la circoncision	 of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not the separation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work voluntarily, especially on children, it is necessary to do the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their law, and we only know what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons performing circumcision in Al-Dal, and with force, and all at once on a newborn; thus the heart flees because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts the upper layer, the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or the healing is delayed, and the pain is doubled, and at the amputation from the shoulder it is not certain whether the tip of the member will be preserved; and at the amputation of the nail by chance the iron may slip away, and the work will run, and many times they are born in such a way that there is no need for amputation.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 From the amputation done at the fleshy part of the thigh, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the flesh cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand and cut equally throughout the entire duration; but let the flesh be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you are only doing to tie the thread around the penis; then comfort him in all ways you can; then hold him straight between your hands, and return the foreskin between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the penis and blow into the foreskin, and pull it up until the head of the penis is in; then clean it well of the accumulated filth, then bind the place tightly with a double thread, then tie it under one finger to another thread; and hold it between the two threads by the second knot at the little finger and ring finger, and cut between the two threads, then lift the foreskin quickly and pull the head of the penis out; then let the blood flow drop by drop, for this is the cure; and apply powder on top and top with a cloth stuck with an egg yolk cooked in rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat with other treatments until healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The shapes of the forces for the anointing are like this: the two heads should be thin and sharp, and the heads should also be as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in the anointing is when the heart inside flees from the incision; then you must extend it to your fingernail, lest the place make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if they pass three days, and what is under the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until that abscess is calmed down, and lightly scrape off the scab; cut as you can move, and beware of the part of the foreskin, for it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure therefore the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if you cut into the heart more than necessary, and it goes further, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 about retaining urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a stone in the bladder, or frozen blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone being in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and let the patient hold his breath as long as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to expel the stone upward, which releases the urine; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called a "syringe," the shape of which is thus: and let it be of fine silver, lightly drawn, like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the urine exiting is such that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head of a wool or cotton bag, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess of the cloth and push it to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a seat, and wash the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis back towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward into the bladder, and the patient feels it approaching the empty space, which is not done unless the channel through which it passes is crooked; then draw out the thread with all the wool bag by bag, and the urine follows the wool, then remove the syringe, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When there are scratches or blood in the bladder, and there is pus collected, and you want to apply distilled water and medicines, do so with all the instrument called a “clepsydra,” and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and has three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see. The place through which the medicine passes should be such that it well stops up the tube without addition, so that no moisture can come out, and push when necessary; and when you want to put your medicines into the bladder, put the end of the enema in the water, and draw with the enema inside. This way, you will draw the moisture into the enema bag, and then push it back strongly inside. The moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema used for enema on the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or horn, and the head is higher; and under the breast where the band falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts strongly with a double thread, and heat the pouch with that moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the pipe, then press your hand on the bladder so that all the moisture flows evenly, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle from it, and pierce it neatly around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like an ale cup, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already said in the division the manners of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between the rainy bladder stones, and all the signs, and which stones one should work on cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stones which are conceived in the bladder happen more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to fine water; and there is sand in the urine, and it swells the patient's penis, and he urinates frequently, then it stops; and after many of these jumps the foundation is laid; and the healing of children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very grave for the elderly, and it is moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes gets in the way of seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and tilt them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes comes out on its own; then have him sit between your hands, and let his hands rest under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then search for it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the area, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall out upon being touched, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and insert it into his anus, and search for the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, draw it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to extend the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the cut is made; then insert the spatula, this is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein; and let it be straight over the stone, and your two fingers should always be at the anus, and the cut should go across so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps this will cause the stone to jump out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: these are eager to come out; and there are those which are below, similar to a hazelnut, and round, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 For those with corners and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not leap out, then you must use pincers which are like a file at the top to tightly squeeze the stone so that it does not escape; or push underneath it a subtle curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot deceive it thus, then widen the hole through which it passed, and if the flesh tears, constrict it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first push the largest into the bladder's neck, then cut above it, then draw it strongly out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must sew it and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 When two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine flows constantly where the wound cannot heal; nevertheless, strive to pull it out, or crush it with pincers, until you extract it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bandage it, and place a damp cloth on top infused with oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bind the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you untie it, wash the place very well with oil and water, then treat it with a fine ointment and a basilica ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if there are abscesses or corrosions and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this urine is retained which exits with the urine: then thrust your finger into the wound and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and make it rotten; afterwards lift the wound with water and honey and oil, and assist him in all ways you know until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind both thighs, and apply medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra and lodged therein, and urine cannot pass; then treat it as I have said before: cut open the urethra many times, and you will be excused from further cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this to be so.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take an iron rod according to this shape and let it be fixed at three angles on one coal:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the rod under the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the rod into the urethra lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand inside the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; then urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is then immediately broken and ejected with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the urethra between the two threads, then pull strongly, and untie the string, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	 of the women's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 Rarely does the stone become lodged in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult, and it is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well enough to reveal to the doctors, especially when she is modest.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone in a woman is more profound than the stone in a man, for which reason a deeper incision must be made, and there is great fear. And if necessity requires it, you must take a skilled midwife, and such is rarely found, and if you cannot find one, do not seek a subtle male doctor; and present her with a wise old woman in the ways of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command regarding the search for the stone; and take great care if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the anus and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must constrain it under her finger, and she should be advised to insert her finger into the vagina of the patient, and seek and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she must move it from grain to grain from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike against the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle of the con, where it is more prepared, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the cut be small at first; then push the reed into the cut, if you feel the stone so tightly that it can come out strongly, and know that there are many types of stones: that is to say, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some with furrows.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know its similarities to understand its outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood overcomes you, put vitriol ointment in its place, and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting stones in humans to help you with your work; and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the cut artery, put the powder on the spot and bind with cloths and bandages, and do not attempt this again, and leave the stone alone, and do not pull it out, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place is darkened, return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	 de hernia carnalis
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 of hernia aquosa is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white sap beneath the skin of the testicles, which contains the sperm; and it is called «sap», and sometimes it is properly in the cloth of the sperm, so that one thinks it is another sperm; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white sap that we have said; and these do not happen unless there is a pox.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the origin of this hernia is from weakness in the testicles, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is yellowish, or redless, or black, or watery white, and this happens most often; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is in the white sap that we have said, then the abscess is reasonable, a long pox like the figure of an egg, and the testicle does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is round with one part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the kidskin and the white silk, then it is felt well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, prove all the introduced instrument, from which the form is made before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows after the introduction, judge that which is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be bled according to his power and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on something not too high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs near the kidneys; then take the small spatula, and cut through the leather of the kidney lengthwise down to the groin, and let your incision be perfectly straight in dividing the leather of the kidney up to the white silk, and peel it carefully as best you can; then pierce the silk with water through a wide hole, and drain all the water, and then put your fingers, and lift the silk upward; but do not touch the kidney itself, only the silk; cut off or in pieces equally the rib on him carefully, for if you do not cut it skillfully, the water will return; and if the egg jumps forcefully at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the silk; then sew together the two lips of the kidney with a stitch, then cure it as other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie,
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 Et si copes la premiere partie com tu as dit; et puis met sur la plaie un pan de laine mouillé en vin, et puis un pan de laine sec, et l'asserres sus au plus près que tu pourras.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Et se tu ne veus mie faire la taille de leu, si met le cautere par dehors sus les coions, et soit eschaufez tout ainsi com nos avons dit.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in every way that you can, until you reach everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more healthy; and beware of incisions bleeding and wounds caused by cutting; and if anything goes against you, whether it be an abscess or bleeding or something else, then cure what goes against you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horribleness, then introduce perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain through the indications we have said that aquous pus is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; pierce the abscess in the lower part with all the wide spatula, and place the perforation along the length of the body; and let the holes be wide, so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the spot, and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining water, then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to exit at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument used to draw water from hydrophobics, whose form we mentioned before; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water will return, and it will be collected after six months or around that time, and when it is collected as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the pustules of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear in many situations, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and the characteristics of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 Therefore, I say that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is very common.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 This is to say, by an acute and feverish superfluity that is spread to the testicles, or from blows; and the color of the abscess varies according to the color of the body; and it does not feel pain, and the abscess is serious; and sometimes there are serious abscesses that are pus-filled and yellowish in color, and sometimes they come from a knot in an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is by swelling of the artery, it is known by the hot abscess, when you press it against your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is made of swelling of the vein is known by its disposition at the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this appearance, and on other signs; and it is that you cut the heart of the abscess, then lift the egg up, and draw out the white pus, and deliver the pouch from all around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already solidified with these signs, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and cut; and if there is air in the pus, or in those who are inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of this air, and cut roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is at the back, then you must cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is done, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a covering similar to a bud, accompanied by the softening of the testicles, and the patient feels very ill when he goes; and the cure for this disease is almost as dangerous as the one mentioned above, nevertheless we will tell you its work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a high seat, then wrap the suspenders of the testicles down to your toes, over all the vessels near the penis, and hold them firmly, stretching them out; then cut with a sharp spatula wide across the vessels, until they are exposed, then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle where there is double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came, and tie again to the other end; then cut straight through the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt fluids; then treat the wound like others where one does not lose any vessels; because by this there is no harm, and if the veins come in all the vessels, it is necessary to draw out the testicles for all the vessels; so that the birds do not lose their nutrition due to the incision of the vessels, dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	 of the rupture of the sinus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The cause of this rupture is due to the cutting or stretching in the abdomen, specifically in the area of the flanks, which causes the intestines to descend from that rupture into one of the testicles; and this rupture occurs either in the sinus or in the stretching of it, and these two types occur for many reasons: from a blow, from a jump, from a fall, from lifting a heavy weight, and similar things; and the sign when it is due to the stretching of the sinus is that it happens gradually, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is even up to its deepest part, because the sinus presses against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is when it is from the section of the abdomen, it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, beneath the skin, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body from the abdomen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the coils go with the intestine, and are retained therein, causing great pain for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these cures of iron, there is fear, therefore one must avoid it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of working is such that you instruct the patient to move the intestine into his hand within the wound, if he can reach it; then let him lie down on his back between your hands, and raise his thighs; then press the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert the hooks of the waist inwards according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the feces can exit; then peel off the abdomen that is beneath the skin of the testicles, so that the white abdomen becomes hard and is exposed on all sides; then insert your finger into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white abdomen that is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second abdomen, and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second abdomen; and then move to the right hand within the heart of the testicles, and raise the white abdomen up to your left hand, and lift the egg with all the abdomen towards the waist; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and loosen what is tied behind the binding; and check with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around the hard white abdomen, and if you find anything, push it down into the belly beneath; then take a needle with a thread made of 10 filaments, each consisting of 10 threads, and insert it into the rear part of the abdomen, which is after the skin of the testicles; after the waist, then cut the heads that appear from the threads, so that there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the abdomen, which we have said is beneath the skin of the testicles, with a strong thread of two parts; then wrap the heads of the threads, and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no servant who tends to it can enter into the holes, where an abscess may come; and put the thread again according to the first long thread, and after these two threads leave the abdomen that is beneath the heart of the testicles the width of a finger; and after everything else according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is beneath the skin of the testicles, so that the urine flows and the feces, as we have said before; then bring moistened wool in oil, and place it in the wounds, and put the thread that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes the white flesh that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often happens, and let the ligature remain until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling off, then be rinsed with hot water, and place what we have said on top of it, until it falls off; then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done like the vein which is near the bladder, in such a way that you tie off the vessels after cutting above lightly below; then cut in half and heal the abscess with what works, until the vessel falls out; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
