Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 When there is a rupture in the intestines, as we have said, the place opens up; and let no one from the intestines fall into the belly, and if any do fall, it is little, and it returns every hour; yet if it stays too long in this state, the wound or fistula grows until the intestines fall out; and this happens by the extension of the fistula which is in the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended, then the place becomes softened and swollen, and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and let the patient lie on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture swollen wide according to the width of three fingers; and then draw out the fistula which is under the skin like the custom, then take the ribbon and put it over the apparent place of the fistula; and press it firmly into the belly, then sew the two apparent places of the fistula on the head of the ribbon, and sew both; then remove the head of the ribbon, and do not cut or extend anything from the fistula or other things, as I have shown you in the cure of the fistula of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the thread, clean it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The syphilis (syfac) is confined and has no appearance in the scar, and the cautery is applied here, being closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the flesh within is softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin on top of the natural skin; then join the two lips together with a single stitch, and if you wish, first sew the excess softened skin firmly with three or four stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and let the thread fall.  />
dou chastrement	 of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that chastisement is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me if I did not speak of it in this book; and there are only two necessary ways: one is that the physician knows how to respond when asked about it and knows the cure; and the other, because we often need the chastisement of certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and dogs and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say then that chastisement is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until the ligaments are softened and drawn out; then take them with your hand until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste,
des hermofrodites	 of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Of hermaphrodites is according to two types in humans: one is that between the two testicles appears as the nature of a woman, with hair, and sometimes it secretes urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other type is in women, who have on the mons pubis like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for the male and female is that you cut off all the flesh, and treat it as other wounds; in the second type, of those whose urine passes through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	 Of leprosy
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Leprosy is a fleshy growth on the natural part of the body, so ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 Il is necessary that you color the superfluity of the tentigene in your hand or in onions, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that blood does not come out, then heal another wound until it is healed; and on a different flesh that arises at the mouth of the marris, and fill it, and perhaps jump far, and it is like a cow, and therefore the ancients called it «maladie kowee».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said about the tentigene, and heal it until it is healed.
de erratique	 Of herring
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 It is called herring when the woman's nature is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has come upon it; or it is due to adjacent flesh, or the subtle or thick humors, and it is made deep in the marris, or on the side, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps also menstruation; and the recognition of this is by the appearance of the hair.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling is clearly visible, it will seek your fingers or toes.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle swelling and it is close to the liver, hurry; do this: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then stretch the two livers very well, so that the subtle swelling is round, and the swelling is above; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie down on her side every day, so that she cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the swelling is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the swelling is from flesh, hang it on a hook and cut it off; and have the blood-stopping medicines ready, like acacia, dragon's blood, incense, with plenty of egg yolk; then apply a wide bandage of lead, so that the wound cannot heal quickly; and thus let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until he is cured.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when flesh grows in the wound, it must be cut according to this manner, unless it is an encysted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For the encysted abscess that is in the wound, one should not do anything to it.
des emorroides	 Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without treatment usually remain so, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thelul; and we have already said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are deeply embedded in the anus and are not felt, should not be treated with a cautery iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Then you must place the woman in a cold room, then grasp the hemorrhoid with pincers, cut its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that restrict blood flow, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding continues, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, let him breathe through cupping glasses on the back and breasts without cutting; then take cloth and moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and let him breathe that place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess rests, then treat the place with oil until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a sharp head, so you must cover it as I have said before; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 of the abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come to the anus, such as chancre and pious abscess and herpes and sty-like sores and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other illnesses that I have spoken of in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes to the breast, which is not one of the abscesses that swell up; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hasten to perforate, but let the matter ripen until the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and have two small chairs where he leans back, and support his back and gather his feet towards the side of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then give him to drink towards the right rib, and bring the instrument that is used to open the breast, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you wish to use this instrument, that you first insert the point in order to know the depth of the breast, so that what enters into the instrument does not go too deep, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the breast with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he place the cone of the instrument above, and that he dip the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one makes an incision with a soft hand, it must be covered at the top with spongy linen cloth; and when the bag is emptied, it should be placed in the wound with moist tents soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil; and place the tent outside the wound at the bottom of the bandage, and place above the bandage and on the wrist a clean cloth moistened in water where the malves have been cooked; then cure it after two days of dressing, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the bandage and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then of water with lily roots and long Aristolochia, cooked well; then return to the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is in the stomach, then you must beware of using iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the natural shape of childbirth, and its sign is when you see a woman press downward and desire to smell air; then you should hasten to help the child out: know that this birth is according to the natural shape, and the issue is under his head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when he descends onto his head, the afterbirth comes out with him, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleaning; and those which come otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Because it sometimes comes upon his feet, and strikes the body or the head, and the hands, or comes upon his stomach, or perhaps his back, and is converted by chance onto his neck, and other evil shapes; thus, it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures of how to help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes upon his head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and the virtue of the child is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, where women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then the nurse places between her teeth the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the afterbirth, and cut it to its fingernail until the moisture that is within flows out; and hold the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with a fennel mixture with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze with cumin, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out strong, then you must gently push them back in little by little; and if they cannot go in, then put the woman on a stool and raise her feet high; then tilt the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when tilting; and if the hands cannot go in, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife mentioned earlier, and extract the child, and push equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the childbirth onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes onto its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then take hold of one foot and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When it jumps up to the hips, instruct her to take hold and make it sneeze with cunnilings; if it jumps further, so be it with God’s will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if it does not jump further as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 For then it goes easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come further as we have said, then take mugwort, oil of cumin, and melted gum; grind all together in a mortar. Then apply this ointment over the woman’s genitals both inside and out. Then make her sit in hot water up to her ribs; and when she is well soaked below, give her a drink of honey wine, and let it sit for an hour. Then seat her on a chair, and make her sneeze by holding her mouth and nose shut, and gently massage her belly, for the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 The issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, let the midwife put her hands little by little; then let it be turned on its back, and let the feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take the hands on top of the belly, and remove the cushions from below, until she is prepared. And if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them strongly, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands there; and draw the child little by little; and instruct the woman to grasp herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 The issue of the child that comes sideways, one hand dangling
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to invent a way to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on the bed and spread her legs widely; then apply the treatment I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, then study bringing back the hand; and look at the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command that she take as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 from the exit of the child on its neck, and with its hands spread, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the nurse takes his hand, then turns it little by little, and looks at it lightly; and when it is equalized, put on the natural treatment of oil and oil, as we have said, then command her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command that she take; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 In this same manner, do so with all the secondary parts
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the force comes this way to all the secondary parts, then cut the secondary part with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child clings to its face and neck, then cut it from the base so that it may not be retained, and let the child die; then put the child back in until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to take some time: then it will easily come out.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an extraordinary thing, but rare.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are an extraordinary thing, and do not live, if at all; I know that they can be many, and are separated by the sinew which divides them, which is attached to the base; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out sharply, then treat them as we have said, and let the bandage be fine, and do it quickly and lightly as she does; and do so that he moves towards safety.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or even more up to fifteen, and all are perfectly formed like a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the bandage know all these things; for by chance similar things may happen, so do according to what is required.
de l’enfant mort	 of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for the dead child or in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work by hand; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution, and has no accident or fear of death. It is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her head bent downwards, and her legs raised; and let the midwife hold two parts, where she lies in bed so that she does not pull during the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint the hands of the midwife with these oils and these mixtures; then insert them lightly into the womb, and seek one place where she inserts the hooks that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is ready to descend onto its head; then insert the hooks into his eyes or his neck or his mouth or on some palate or under the beard or in the vagina or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, then insert them into the palm and between the ribs; and it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand, and put the curve between her thumb and index finger of the left hand, and let her insert all her hand lightly, and insert the hook in any of these places we have said, until it comes to the empty place; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 then insert one against the other, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then move them equally from side to side, in order to move out, and let the thorns be pointed to hold on, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, then grease the ball of your thumb with oil and push it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if nothing remains, place this thorn in a higher spot, and do this until all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it in a cloth until all comes out; then cut off at the joint of the foot or the knee, and thus you should do with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if there is sharp water collected at the top, then you must insert a spatula between your fingers, split the skull, and extract the water; or rotate the instrument called "almidach," from which the form comes with the instruments in the following chapter; and do the same thing if the child has an unusually large head naturally. Then draw out the bones with the tongs, and if the head protrudes and is tight around the pelvic brim, it should be split until the water that is in the lower part of the birth canal comes out; and if it cannot come out, strike it in pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, then you must puncture until the water flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is on his feet, then the traction is gentle, and the reduction at the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is stuck in the belly or the breast, you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is there drains out; and if the other members are removed, and only the head remains, then press your hand deeply into the womb, and pull it up to the mouth of the womb; then insert one or two fingers, and pull strongly; and if the mouth of the womb is narrow due to a hot abscess that has formed there, you should not struggle, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and administer poultices, and use softening and moistening liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then do as we have said with the living child; and if one cannot, then draw out the fetus piece by piece, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for abscesses that come in the womb; and if blood comes out, put her in cold water restraining, and give other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then another grew on top of that one, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time, she got an abscess in the womb, which swelled so much that it burst open, and began to be very putrid.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I applied a strong attracting plaster, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was very amazed by this, because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I examined the wound and drew out many bones until the woman was in better condition; and the woman lived for a long time like this, and there always came out a little pus from that place; and I have noted down this chapter only because when the master finds something strange, he should know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 To bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Here comes the form of the press, with which one moves the weights; and at two turns, the two keys of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 However, the horns should be more subtle of the restricter, and made of ivory or boxwood; and the mouth of the stick should be two thumbs wide, and the margin of the trees one thumb, and in length one palm and a half; and between the two levers there should be two adjustments of this same stick, which are fixed at one end and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are pushed into the mouth of the bone to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 A different form, more subtle and lighter, should be made from the wood of an ebony or box tree, resembling pliers; and it should have at its two heads two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vulva with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet dangling and legs spread, then insert the two adjustments close together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand over the entire instrument, just as you have done with the pliers, according to the quantity by which you wish to open the mouth of the vulva, until the vagina does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument is all surmounted, and their resemblances are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, so much the more urgent is the work, and higher for men because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not disregard the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze strongly, and press your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she expels it by this means, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the womb of the woman, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be cooked in water on the fire. Then place a reed in the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapor enters into the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 If the ligament tears quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and is not weakened, then instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand in oil of cicely or muslin cloth with vinegar, and then place it on the wound, and seek the ligament; and when she finds it, take hold of it and gently stretch it little by little until the wound does not swell at the stretching; but you must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; then it will come out and relax.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the wound is tightly constricted, we have said the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not come out from all that we have said, then take care not to be hasty in pulling; but it is necessary for whoever is at the mouth of the wound, that you tie him to the thigh of the woman, then administer an enema with four-component oil mixture; then she will fart and restore, and come out stronger; but nevertheless, when she farts, bad odor comes to the stomach and the head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 If it is therefore necessary, fumigations are appropriate for this: some of the ancients have proven fumigations of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The form of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman for the retention of flowers and the second stage is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it is made of glass similar to a tube, and one places the subtle end in the nature, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be over the coals, and continue until it is consumed, and then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	 to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born with the anus not pierced, but rather blocked by a subtle membrane: it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and do not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and be careful that she does not touch the linen; then place a cloth moistened in wine and oil on top, then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not pop out, then put in the opening a piece of lead, and leave it there for fewer days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this blockage comes from a sudden vein or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that sudden [bleeding]: if it is treated, as we have said about the piece of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	 Of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from below the anus are nodules, and growths that come beside the anus towards the outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and attracts abundant white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are painful; and they are known by this: that during defecation or flatulence, some come out, and occasionally one comes out in a rush.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the midpoint of the penis; they extend to the junction of the thigh, and to the navel of the vulva.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows the fistula penetrating to the anus, and not penetrating: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and thrust a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no convolution.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is convolution, then thrust a subtle tent of lead or a horsehair, as much as you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, nor does egestion, ventosity, or vermiform appendix come out, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the passage of the urine, then the urine escapes from it, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated up to the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the location of the pain around it, then it constantly flows out, and neither medicines nor healing by ointment are effective; and in these perforating fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and foolish physicians waste their efforts on them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In those that are not perforating and not old, there is hope of health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger inside, and if you sense that the tent has been pierced; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the syphilis or the flesh, then know that it is perforated; so do not try to heal it, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Nevertheless, one can heal some [cases] well, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one provides is to heat the cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and insert it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times, so that you know these fleshy parts have burned, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cure the wet tents with butter, until those fleshy parts come out, then cure the ointment, joining flesh and suturing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If this is not another way to be healed; and if the tent enters but does not perforate until the finger that is in the fundament, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue, and you see the fistula at the end of the covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and always push the tent forward, and afterwards apply cautery until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then remove those fleshy threads that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing should remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you, and it passes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Because the fire cautery combines two good things: namely, the burning of these hairs nearby, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of wet tents with butter or crushed substances, until the place swells up, and the burned hairs come out in the swelling; then treat the wound with hardening ointments, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if the fistula reaches all the way to the bottom of the anus and is separated from the body, then place your finger in the anus and seek it out.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and there is the tissue or silk or hair in it, which is close to perforating, do not proceed further unless there is hope and expectation through the use of one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it to the bottom, or if possible place a tent and treat it as before; but do not go too deep, lest you cut the support that holds the anus, and cause involuntary defecation; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut near the anus, either by tent or by another suitable instrument; then cleanse the faulty hair that is in the wound, as much as you can; then endeavor to restore the wound, and make the fistula remain on the outer part of the anus: this will be less difficult for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fissures occur in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fissure, and it is on the side of the anus near the skin above, then take a punctured tent at the top in this form.
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And you push a twisted thread into it, and push the tent with all the thread into the fissure until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is protruding within the margin of the anus, then extract the thread from that hole, just as you push your finger into the anus; and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and press them against each other, and leave it for one day or two; and constrict it occasionally, until the thread cuts through those tissues that are between them, and they fall off; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 If the fistula does not open, then make it open in all the ways you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it is not right to cover for the healing so deeply, and then heal, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here.
des emorroydes	 hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are in two ways: either they are inside the rectum like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and blood always comes out of them, and there is one or more, and they are outside the rectum and at the edge of the rectum; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh. And the cure for those who have them inside the rectum is that you instruct the patient to sit on the toilet until the rectum comes out, and the threads appear; then hurry, and clamp it with pincers, or hold it with your nail, then cut off its roots; and if the nails cannot hold them because of the moisture, then take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of flannel; and pull with your fingers, then cut, and sprinkle some warm powders that are suitable for cauterization on top; or you cauterize as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure with other cures until it is healed; and if the rectum cannot come out, then enema the patient with a bitter and sharp enema to clean what is in the rectum so that it can come out openly. When the patient sits and the threads are out of the rectum, the cure is light; and it is that you take them with your nail or pincers, and cut, then cure as we have said, until it is healed, and that it fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is necessary for you to perform the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread, insert it into a needle, then pull the thread through and make the needle pierce from the other side; turn the two ends of the thread underneath the needle, making sure it is wide enough; then tighten the thread firmly, knot the thread, remove the needle, and do this with all the others, leaving one for draining excess blood; then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or wax over the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and leave it until they heal, and once healed, treat them with ointment and other treatments until they are cured.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 of dryness from the intestines or the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Many times dryness occurs in the intestines, due to natural constraints, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must scrape off the skin above with a spatula or your nail, not allowing it to moisten; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry, repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it bleeds profusely and is raw; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	 from trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Formication is a small, hairy creature that enters the body and goes very deep; sometimes the cold finds it, and one feels it like death from trembling, and it spreads throughout the whole body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is such that you take a quill of a goose feather, or a strong quill of an ox, and place that quill on the trembling part, until the circle surrounds the entire trembling part; then turn your hand around the entire quill so that it covers the entire trembling part, and insert it deeply, and eradicate the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see this, do it with a quill of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be subtle below and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 nor should it be perceived, to better hold the two together, and better press them And if you see this, then cauterize the trembling part, as is written in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes one makes an enema with silver or gold, or melted iron or copper; and sometimes it is made from these instruments, both small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those who prepare for the treatment of children who are weak and suffering should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The form of the small and large enema is such that it is wide at the top where the intestines are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there should be an opening where the intestines are tied as you see, and the tip should be perforated; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and the bag where one puts the medicines should be made from a beast's bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one finger's width of space, then insert into these holes a strong thread of twisted silk in the shape of an X or O, and assemble the bag like this, and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and that is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg white, or a similar substance, then insert it lightly; then the minister should press with his two hands together until it is all empty, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, then hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps through the night, then there is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you give an enema for a disease of the intestines, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are in the rectum or abscess, then let the enema be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin enema on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines according to the method.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by falling of a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or by a lance, or a club, or an arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or the buttocks, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because their treatment will be in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then beware if it is from the fall of a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it cauterized immediately with cephalic caustic even if there is little blood from the wound, and let the cautery be on the opposite side of the injured part; and let the patient avoid overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be cauterized, let him eat less food, and drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked only in rose oil or stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the fresh wound, as long as it bleeds all its blood, and is not moved by the air, a powder that I will tell you a little later; and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut or similar, and the lips of the wound cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by sewing, as I will say for wounds in the belly, with the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed bone and gaping, and holds together only by a thread, then cut it off; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse food, such as heads and cooked wheat, also like beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rottenness in the skin that reaches to the bone, then cut away all the rot and throw it away, then treat (the wound); and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which does not stop bleeding with medicine, then seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, bind it with a thread; and if this does no good, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder which binds before the heat has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is thus: take one part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind it finely, and fill the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with quicklime alone, when one has neither frankincense nor dragon's blood, but that the heat has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has moved the wound, especially in summer, do not put this powder on it at all; but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it weeps; then proceed to other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, draw it out with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	 of a neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, unless a nerve of the neck or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other device than to leave the treatment alone and put nothing constricting on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be below, as hot water in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and also washed in soft water, and other stones of the same kind according to this manner, and moist ointments.
