Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then open it in a lower place; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows out, then dry it off, bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the windpipe or the throat is cut, and the passage is preserved, through which food goes, then sew up the throat on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape; and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then open it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them out completely if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound suppurates, and let the opening be drained and cleansed; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle the powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife wound, and the wound is deep, observe if there is swelling in the wound as the patient lies down: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it so that blood does not seep deeply, return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply drawing ointment, and bandage it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will be no spasm, nor heart tremor or strangulation of breath; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat it with tents and other treatments until it is healed; if it cannot be healed, and works, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, whether worse or on the back, treat it like those in front; if it is large, with stitching; if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone and has chipped pieces, cleanse the wound, and draw out the splinters if they are loose; if they are not loose, let the wound fester, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 From the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines come out, causing their exit; and the sewing up is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is harder to put the intestines back in if they are not replaced hot on hot; because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, so they go back in less easily. And for this reason, the medium wound is worse, because it is more difficult to return the intestine to its place than in others. And know that the treatment of the belly is according to four methods: two common sewings occur in the sewing of the belly, and the sewing of other wounds of the body, and two other specific sewings are common with other wounds; nevertheless, they are more specific with the sewing of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and something of the intestines has come out, it is a very difficult thing to put back, which can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm the intestines in this manner: moisten one sponge or piece of linen in hot water only, and cook in boiling water cinnamon and pepper and cloves; and rinse the intestine until the swelling has subsided; sometimes this wine restricts, and it is better alone for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water where althea and mallows have been cooked, for by this the opening is made easier; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first care is better than cutting, no one should cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split it: cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened and the intestines jump out, then put them back inside according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And when the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and the chest higher than the parts below, and likewise if the break of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to this so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must treat as I say both large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what you have prepared, then take between your hands the pious minister who holds all the instruments in his hand, and gather the lips; and this is the common manner of suturing, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' width from the head of the wound, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is underneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and gather the two heads of the siphac together in four; then tighten a double thread around the needle on two sides, then gather the two lips of the wound together in the same way, and then leave two fingers' width, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this with the needles until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and thick, for subtle needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium-sized; it is also not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and work the wound before the suturing; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put tenths or cloths on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one can use a needle or two in the second suturing, which is common, and it is that you gather the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the siphac together in one needle where there is good medium-strength thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, then remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes; and put space between each suturing the thickness of a small finger; this suturing is known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and the intestines protruded well two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought him back the intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed for fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put on the wound old cotton twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and insert it from outside to inside; when it has pierced the skin straight on, leave the head of the thread where you inserted the needle, and make it come out the other side from inside to outside; and the meaning of this sewing is that you sew just like furriers sew furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side and take it back on the other, until the entire stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen describes specifically, is done as some do: they naturally bring together the two parts and apply one head of the needle to the other head in this manner: insert a needle into the head of the mirror nearby, and make it pierce only that place, leaving the two heads of the needle; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part until inside, to the two heads of the needle; then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part until inside, in two other holes of the mirror which are on the opposite side; and this is the most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens says these words, and some testify to it: that one should stitch the belly with two needles, with a thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, the stitching must be larger than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then you should resume the burning inside and on the skin; then apply the powder healing flesh, and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointment that is available, until the wound closes; and stitch the threads, and let the seams and the mirach heal; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then apply, as soon as it begins to cast pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 Car you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may affect the principal members, then you must wet a light linen cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and wrap it around the corners and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or infection in his bowels, and this often happens, then give him an enema of black wine tede, and likewise if the infection reaches the intestines; perforate it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the thinness of the veins there, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the gut spills from the wound, replace it like the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must tie the place that is black to prevent blood from flowing therein, for there are veins and arteries; then cut that which is between the ligature, and hang the two ends depending from the lower part of the wound until it falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 from the wound's edge
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is cut and the wound is small, it can be healed in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and from it came excrement and windiness; I treated it as best I could, and did not cease to care for him until he was healed, and the place healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sewn, I feared that the patient might have pain in his stomach; but there was no pain, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner: take large-headed pins, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on top of the two lips so that it pulls its mouth up; and then cut off the head, and this is done so that it cannot come loose, then place another pin afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely enclosed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and the head becomes attached in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be tied off with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestinal thread which should be very thin, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and draw it together; and this method of sewing is not outside the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal parts, there is no cleverness or skillfulness, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 From a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it bursts open, is universally called a "fistula," and likewise when it opens and pours out pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is by definition a hard and white nodule without pain, and it opens like the feather of a bird; sometimes it discharges clear pus, other times thick; sometimes little, other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the section on wounds, that any wound that does not heal, and there is no flesh, it is only healed through one of the nine causes: that is to say, due to the scarcity of blood or body; or because of its corruption; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the edges, which prevents new flesh from growing; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for healing; or because the corruption is in the form of plague; or due to the nature of the region where digestion is slow, and healing is delayed, and it swells naturally; or there are veins or bones. And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the section on wounds.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or I must inform you of the treatment for a fistula caused by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and the arteries, and the nerves, or the sinuses, or the intestines, or the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and there are those that come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of serious condition, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you wish to know it, then take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek it with a subtle probe of boxwood, for boxwood bends more easily around the crookedness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then seek it wisely as you can, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and it is deeply rooted, and inquire carefully of the patient about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned to you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove firmly the foul matter and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from a right place, then it is necessary that you cut deeply, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in aquatic medicine, and pour them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluous material that remains at the bottom; and then put on healing ointments, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve strikes a main joint, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, so boil it until all the corruption is removed, then treat with things that enclose flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and it opens again as before, know that you have not reached the source: uncover and seek until you reach the source, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it heals thus, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other strategy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with tongs, pull it out with an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving not one; and if moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, cut off flesh and moisture and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something causing putrefaction on the wound, and let it be until the place is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will break more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, raise only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then suture the wound; and if there is a great part of the putrefaction and it reaches to the marrow of the bone; then you must saw and cut all the way to the putrefaction, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 It was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause until the matter reached the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no outward sign for opening; but the physicians, through their folly, worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and many matters came out of it, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings from which all threw pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians attended to him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, until I was called there, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what came out through the openings at a great rate; and the youth's flesh became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some went against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the holes until I exposed part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption went as far as the inside of the bone; I removed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except what I removed; and I began to treat the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but it could not heal; then I tried again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then worked on healing the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm’s width of the bone, and drew it out completely, then treated it with medicines; and it was healed and healed quickly, and there was no need to repeat the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation of blood he often bled, but was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrariety at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sutured in this manner: take a linen thread and bind it to the end of the bone that is open; and command someone to extend it upwards; and put another thicker linen thread over the first thread, and tie it on the flesh above the bone, and stretch the head, so that you draw the corrupt flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to suture, so that the stitch does not hurt the flesh; and place a hot ember or a board under the bone to melt the corrupt flesh; and it must be sutured as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and also sutured again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, and put a coal underneath, puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, then saw from one part of the corruption to the other; et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, and let the length of the saw be a thumb's width longer than the corruption, as we have said; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, if the corruption is in the joint, si cope la jointure corrumpue, then cut away the corrupt joint, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part, and saw through the bone where it contains the other part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper, there is no alternative but to cut; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, ou ou poignil dou piet, or in the ankle, si est mout fort celle chose, this procedure is very challenging, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; and you must investigate that corruption to see how it opens up; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, but cleanse it in all the ways you can, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire, except that the vein or nerve does not interfere; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, and know that there are many instruments for cutting these bones, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, and their thickness and fineness, et lor grandor et lor petitece, and their size and smallness, et lor duresce; and their hardness; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument, therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, selonc la conissance de cest art, according to the knowledge of this art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.
dou feu	 of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head rots from within or without; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to amputate that member up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the lack of the member; and the sign is that the member turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, then this corruption of the member goes from member to member, and takes over the whole body; so hasten with the amputation, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous animal, such as a sea scorpion or viper and the like, if the corruption is at the base of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and no treatment will help except the quantity of its virtue; and do the same when the corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or tying the member is such that you tie it above and below, and one assistant extends one of the ties downwards, and another assistant the other tie upwards, and you cut the flesh between the two ties to a width of one finger, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or tie, and place on each side a piece of linen, so that the ligature does not touch the healthy area, and thus the patient may receive another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you work, cauterize the area immediately, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in one of his feet: he had a blackness that resembled a burn from fire, and that corruption first came into his foot's toe, so much so that it spread throughout the entire foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and a long time later the corruption returned to the toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repressive things after cleansing the body, but could not stop the corrosion; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, because I hoped to repel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have not told this story except so that others may learn from it, if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 A certain time comes an abscess in a fleshy place, and it stays so long that it forms a large swelling of the boil; and then it thunders and bursts, and the pus jumps out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel; and the skin that is above is as thin as a delicately woven cloth, and it does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve; and such an illness is called «sinus», and it is not called «fistula»; but if it extends so far that it reaches to the bone in depth, then it is called «fistula»; and the skin is such that you can cut all around that skin, even when it is thin, just like a cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you think that the skin is swollen, and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it thus: observe whether the breast is large, and the opening from which it issues is of foul odor; then catheterize with Egyptian medicine made like this: take equal amounts of asphaltum, oil, and lead oxide, and cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and catheterize the breast, and constrict the opening; and let the medicine remain inside for two hours, then remove by pressing out; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the corruption is removed; sometimes catheterize with ashes water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take vine wood ashes, and pour water over them, then strain it, and catheterize until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes water, then catheterize with water and honey in which there is a little lead oxide mixed; or you can catheterize with honey and mead, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the mead makes the flesh dry; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well cleansed, then catheterize with what causes flesh to grow in it, and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can catheterize with some medicines and onions, whose properties I have spoken of in the treatise on onions; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the catheter cannot enter, then widen it slightly with an iron, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up except for one place where the catheter can enter, and if the opening from which the matter issues is at the top, then cut lower than that place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the abscess is ripe, do not allow any flesh to enter; and if you cannot cut the skin underneath as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the abscess runs to the lowest place there is, for when the abscess is ripe, no flesh should enter. And if you cannot cut the skin underneath as you wish, prepare it so that the abscess runs lightly downwards and leaves nothing of the abscess; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut strongly towards the hole in the skin, wider than before, then extend a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to lighten the abscess, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once. And the one that is on the hole of the skin, take off often to remove the abscess, and know what comes out of the abscess, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not. And when your medicine has thus spread and you see the nature that leaps up on the hole of the wound, know that the skin is already healed, and health approaches; and then unbind in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the chest throws out undigested matter after many days, know that the chest does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison follows after a long time, do not despair of your health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are men whose flesh grows slowly in their wounds, and others do the opposite; and if undigested matter comes out of the chest after many days, know that the chest does not heal; and if the chest is slow to heal and distant, then use dry medicines which are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as ointment defined, for there is a great deal of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take ointment defined, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with equal parts old wine; then cook it and use it; and this same thing does better when cooked and thickened, if ointment defined is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; and then glue a cloth onto it, and place it on the chest; and sometimes add long aristolochia, and celestial lily roots, which are like vetch flour and centaury; and use both simple and compound ones: grind them, and make them into powder, and put them over the honey I mentioned earlier, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone or hard parts or limbs; then treat it as a cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 Of the abscess of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Paronychia is an abscess that occurs beneath the fingernail of the hand or foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it becomes old and is not treated, a foul abscess forms there, spreading and throwing pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps all the way through it; and there is decay reaching the bone, causing fetid pain, and the head of the finger is swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut away with an iron all the remaining excess of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is intact. And if the nail presses into the flesh, begins to prick, and wounds it, then you must place the blade under the nail that points at the flesh, and push it up, and delicately and lightly cut off that flesh; then apply burning and corrosive medicines on the rest of the flesh to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone is there, it cannot heal. And if you see the finger begin to rot, cut it off at one of the joints as said before, then cure until healed; and if it is struck and swells and feels great pain, it is necessary that you cauterize it first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by slicing across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain. And if it happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two thumbs that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is one with bones, and sometimes there is one with a nail, and sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, and their birth is in the noses of some people.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any knuckle of the thumb does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the thumb may possibly move; the shape of the fleshy one is light, like this: cut it off at its root with a wide spoon-like tool.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 The one that grows in the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore, be cautious.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In one who is born or should at the anus, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The union that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Then you must cut that union, so that the parts return to their natural forms; then place between two tents or cloths moistened with rose oil, so that they do not join together; or you place between two thin lead plates, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If union occurs to one of his fingers with the palm, cut that union as necessary.
des vils	 of the wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Wounds are large swellings full of melancholic superfluities that come in many members of the body; and they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer purging with cinnamon, and then heal it with balm.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is done in two ways: one is to cut the wounds and draw out the black blood; and the other way is to lift the wound and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The cutting is done in this manner: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large vein is thinned out; then hold the patient's leg from above the hip down to the part below the knee; then cut the wound in one place, or two, or three, making a wide cut; then lift it and draw out the black blood forcefully by hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can bear; and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that generate black bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the wounds are full, and this benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The raising of it is according to this manner: raise the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and pour hot water on the leg until it becomes red, and swell the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, then cut along the length from the knee to the ankle; then lift the skin with tweezers, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the vein down, so that it is raised from the skin, and then slightly pinch with tweezers, then cut in another place higher by three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift to the tweezers, as you have done before, and pinch in another place higher by two fingers; then make another cut, or several if you need them, then lift and pinch at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second cut; then draw from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a needle with a very strong double thread, and tie and pull, and insert below the vein, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and take care that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then one cannot pull or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, then put moistened wool in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to cut the face is curved and does not slice, so that it cuts the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is injected in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in land without moisture; and perhaps it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body, snakes and worms, injected between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the vein opens, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of linen from one and a half to two cubits, and the knot, and let the linen hang at the leg. And every time that some blood exudes from lack of strength, then wrap around it the linen and the knot; and if it is too long, then cut part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until all of it has come out. For if you cut it, then it enters into the flesh and brings an abscess and rottenness to that place, and a bad illness; because of which thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and that nothing remain in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated from five palms long, or ten, and one man came to me whose (vein) issued ten palms long. And when you cut it, then it releases a finger's worth of pus, and pierce it until the bottom, so that all comes out; and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and apply to the place medications preventing rottenness each day, then heal it as (you would) an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there are few grains, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many grains come out from there; heal it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and it goes through the whole body up and down, and one feels it well when moving from member to member, until it pierces the skin where it goes, and jumps out; and it comes from the putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, serpents, leeches, and ascarids in the stomach; and one fears its malice, because when it goes through the body, if it goes to the head and comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being healed and pulled, one cannot do so unless it is going: therefore, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong, tight ligature, then cut above and pull strongly; and if the pus has entered deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire above until it dies. And the greatest harm it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head of the eye, hold firmly under it the sorcil, then cut above and pull strongly. And the patient should use body cleansing with dissolving medicines for bad humors causing putrefaction, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain which comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our country "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from one member to another; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise up to the shoulder as quickly as anything, like living silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain left that place and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a short while later it ran through the entire body, until it came into the other arm; then she told me that it was always turning around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 Je m'étonnais beaucoup comment elle passait ainsi d'un membre à l'autre, car je n'avais jamais vu cette maladie de cette façon.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Cependant, j'avais vu beaucoup de personnes ressentir des douleurs d'une partie du corps à une autre, mais je ne l'avais jamais vue de cette manière, comme je l'ai vu chez la femme; et je me suis dit que c'était parce que les femmes ont un corps sec, et les veines découvertes, et pour cette raison apparaissent ces ventosités contraintes; mais on ne les voit pas de cette manière chez ceux qui sont délicats, et qui ont des corps humides et des veines remplies.
