Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the wax cloth, and apply a poultice made of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then place the bandages; and let the bandage on the break always be stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have VI bandages on the arm in several arrangements: whether the break is in one of the bones or in two; and tighten more above the break than elsewhere, and always less when extending, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And after some days, restore the limb and the ligament.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if some bad thing happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you must rinse the limb with hot water until the itch is calmed; and let the limb rest not tightly wrapped.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the splinting, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone dislocated, and similar things, treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And take care that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight; then you must soften it in a cup, and let it rest like this for some days until the nourishment flows there, and then splint it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 Et si nul de ces choses que nous avons dites ne vient au malade, si ne le délier pas jusqu'à vingt jours.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And when around it, then he can put his hands on his neck, and his necks should be equal, and he should avoid movement and turning, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 Of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that at the back of the hand and near the fingertips, there are few breaks, and it only happens as a result of frequent bending.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright facing him evenly; then place his hand on a flat surface, and let the assistant straighten the broken bones, and let the physician align them well until they are properly joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there is no abscess, then place a splint according to the size of the location; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the abdomen on the side of the plant, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken side; and then bind with a long cloth, and let the end be as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the forearm, you must place a bandage on top and another underneath the limb, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the arm, and secure the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break is in any of the fingers, whether it is a thumb or not, place it straight; and bind it with the hand, and if you see it, place a small straight bandage to lift the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is in other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; either bind them all together as best you can, or place a bandage on top, as for the thumb; and take care in the restoration and placement of an abscess, and support whoever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 From a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and this can be seen when it turns forward or backward; the restoration consists in tying a ligament above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches their ligament to an equal extent; this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And so if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be next to the knee, and the extension downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone equally in both hands until it follows its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bandage, unless pus comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside before returning to your work and treatment; the plaster is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 And it is necessary that you wrap around the break I bandage doubled in II or III, and remove the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the nail, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and the ends of the thread come up; then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then place on the break splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to evenly distribute the pressure, then begin to bind strongly III or IV times on the break; and as you go higher on the break, bind less; then tie II ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie III splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, so that you come near the foot; and bind it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, provided that there is no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and address what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then one should remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then one must split the place, and pull strongly; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that splints are put there, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in this kind of restoration the patient does not become lame.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in about 40 days, or a little less or more, according to the different constitutions of the body.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 Of the ankle of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the ankle of the knee there are few fractures, but it often swells.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, then it is only a split or a puncture, and this occurs in all wounds, and in those without wounds, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the treatment is to join together equally that which is broken with its two parts, as much as possible; then apply a poultice, and put on it a round bandage, if you need one, and bind it as needed, then follow all the preparations that we have said for other fractures, such as abscesses or others; so treat each accident with what is necessary until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is rightly called «mustelz», and the other is called «foscile»; and all kinds of fractures occur as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the workings are all alike. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible; and it turns downward.  /> Ensi de coi que il soit de li dui os brisiez.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is ugly, and there are many fragments, then the traction should be less and gentler; and set it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no break, but sometimes there is a break in the foot bones and in the two hollows, and it happens more often as a fracture in several places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is a break in the foot bones and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the sick person's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and now put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply a poultice and bandages on top, and under the sole of the foot put a small board with two full nails, then bind the foot firmly, and after you have wrapped cloths around it and other necessary things.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 Et quant trois jours ou quatre seront passés, si desserre le lien, car tu trouveras les os égaux, qu'ils soient cassés ou disloqués.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 Et s'il y a un os brisé parmi eux, alors restaure-le, comme nous l'avons dit pour les doigts de la main; puis mets une épingle sur l'os brisé selon sa longueur, et qu'elle soit un peu plus large. Ensuite, place sous le pied cette planche que j'ai mentionnée, et serre-la fermement; et s'il y en a deux ou trois, ou plus, qui sont brisés, alors mets une épingle sur chaque os selon sa taille, enveloppée dans un morceau de lin, et serre la planche sous le pied. Et qu'elle soit placée au-dessus du chef de la planche, hors du ventre du pied, pour bien le maintenir.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each incident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the break of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the wrist bone of the woman is broken, have her sit enlarged, then incline it towards the back, and hold it from behind; then fill the gap in the woman's nature with cotton, and put as much as a fistful inside; then make the woman stand up, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton jumps until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone comes back with the fistful; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or so: the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and attach a reed to the opening, and fill the entire bladder in the nature; then blow into the reed very strongly, so that the bladder swells inside: the nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bones of the wrist of the man or woman are broken, restore them as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who study and practice this, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a fracture indicates in many cases the right way of restoration; pay attention to it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's windpipe and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it there for three days or as long as necessary, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be treated now, as the treatments that we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound is clean, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then immediately restart to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, unless there are abscesses like those.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if abscesses like those come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about evil accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone appears on the surface of the wound exposed, then it is necessary that you place it lightly and carefully with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extension is not ready to place it evenly with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument that has VII or VIII fingers in length, and its width according to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary for the physician to have III or IIII, according to what he needs for each fracture cure; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," for which the curved head should be placed on top of the protruding bone; and push once, until it returns, and are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut off with an appropriate instrument, either a knife or scissors, according to your ability; then remove that which remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is not in its place, then moisten the bandage in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is summer; and do not put any oily substance on the wound, such as cerate or other things, so that it does not cause rot and corruption; then administer estelles when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be well cautious that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times the foolish physicians have done this, and have brought about death or corruption in the patient; and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that a bad accident may occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to apply sponges; but wrap around, in place of sponges, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two that the wound becomes hotter, then remove everything that you have put on at all times, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, such as tetrapharmakon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bone slides down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but the bone slips back again, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must search the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula occurs in the place, or another form of corruption, then you must cure it according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and protrudes from the limb, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it out, for many times death results, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out on its own after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 Of the bruises that come upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see this after the healing of the bruise, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is unsightly; and by chance the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Take heed therefore if the sore is fresh: and administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others; and whether you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with stiptic wine or a lot of egg or with honey; and apply to the knot in poultices, and bind it well, and do not unbind for many days; and then unbind, and begin another until the swelling is removed; or you bind upon a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already hardened like stone, and it must be removed, cut off the top, and bring out the superfluous part; or you can scrape it with some razor until it is removed, and treat until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the bone fracture is healed, and afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as needed; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of excessive bleeding; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because the person has little blood in their body, and thus the limb is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is to make the patient eat and soften their body until their blood increases; and administer baths and bring joy and cheer; then apply poultices on the limb so that the poultices attract abundant nourishment, and often wash it with warm water so that the nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 Of the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the whole limb anew; many foolish physicians have done this in our land. And these works are blamed, and great evils come from them, and perhaps death. However, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, they must be washed with hot water, or cooking herbs that soften, such as leaves of comfrey, roots, mallow, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, well made with diachylon, and take the juice of comfrey, and cook it with goose fat or sesame oil, and place the plaster on top. Or you take fresh figs, and grind them with marshmallow powder, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes dislocation is removed by continually and extensively rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let the limb be moved gradually each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the distortion is swollen and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be cut down to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and apply caution and skill in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 A dislocation is an exit of some joint from its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misshapen, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When a dislocation happens to someone, it must be immediately brought back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car si l’on tarde, le lieu s’enfle, et par aventure on ne peut remettre la partie à sa place; c’est pourquoi il ne faut pas déplacer la partie quand elle est gonflée : souvent cela cause des spasmes et d'autres douleurs ; néanmoins, quand cela arrivera, faites saigner le malade, puis laissez-le jusqu’à ce que l’abcès soit apaisé; ensuite, appliquez sur le membre de l’eau chaude et de l’huile, puis réajustez légèrement, et soignez chaque membre selon comment il reviendra à sa place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 Et j'ai ordonné les chapitres sur les dislocations de la tête aux pieds.
des mandibules	 Of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It often happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly removed from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and the saliva flows from the mouth so that it cannot be held, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is enveloped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is slight, it returns to its place by itself in many ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and whole, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the servant holds the patient's head, and the physician places a little cloth of one of his hands at the base of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other two hands be free to make it even; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the physician sets it straight until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the setting is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, then soak them in hot water and oil until they are easily set; do not delay the setting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are set evenly and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then place wet compresses on cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two pillows so that it is not moved to the right or left, nor should they make an effort to speak, but take light food until the pains are removed and the jaws are bound; and then he may chew what he wishes lightly, and should not struggle to open his mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two mandibles cannot be set in place at once within an hour, and are not converted to their proper places, fever and sudden constipation will ensue, and possibly diarrhea, and perhaps pure bile will be vomited.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times he who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The fork cannot dislocate from the inside of the chest or from the pelvis, and it is sometimes dislocated from the finger, which can be felt distinctly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms; then press firmly on the place with your palm, and it will return; then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it tightly; and the joint towards the armpit cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus also is restored the shoulder joint when it has been separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates at the lower part of the armpit; and the second is at the chest part; and sometimes it dislocates at the upper part, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it jumps quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men to have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and he thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary that you test it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it is down towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the shoulder blade on the back the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly on the back; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the caregiver lifts the patient's hand up, then places his fingers underneath, and lifts the joint forcefully upwards in place; and the caregiver lifts the hand and stretches it upwards, then places it underneath; thus it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within many days after, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and let the caregiver prepare a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and mallow in water, and apply it; then let the patient be laid on their back, and place under the joint an even pad of linen, not too soft nor too hard; then let the healer place his heel on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the patient; and another caregiver holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; that shoulder will return immediately now, and if you see this happen then reset according to this manner: and it is that you make a man present who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight by the side, and place his shoulder under the patient's joint, and lift the joint upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another caregiver pulls the hand of the patient downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, let him carry something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And one can also reset it in another way: and it is that you drive a long stick into the ground, such that its tip is as round as a pestle, nor too thick nor too thin; then let it be placed under the patient, but that he has soft cloths above, and the patient should stand along the length of the stick; then his hand should be stretched out on the other side in the same manner, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick of two arms' length and four fingers' width, which has a rounded head to enter deeply under the armpit, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then place the patient under the top of a draped post, so that the post does not hurt the patient. Place it below the patient's seat; extend some of your arms along the length of the post, and tie the shoulder to the post, with the arm at the top of the hand. Then put the arm on the top step of a wide ladder, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: now we return to the joint.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when she is inside, in whatever manner it may be, you must place below the seat a round piece of wool, then put the plaster prepared with flour from the mill, along with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then press it firmly under the seat, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he takes little food, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then take more after V or VII days, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is displaced from its place due to moisture that has come upon it, or for any other reason, then you must apply cauteries to three openings, as was said before in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after VII days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm above, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation that occurs towards the foot and the breasts, or the rear, is caused by pushing and stretching of the hands, and other means are administered; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after the healing there is stiffness in the member, and delay in movement, then the patient should bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the rib
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the rib joint is easily dislocated and easily returns; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired, for one can see and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick cut with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated, and the arm cannot be bent, nor can it reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And you must reset it before any abscess forms there, for if an abscess were to form, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and sometimes death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the reset is done this way when it can be reset: you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arm be stretched out, and the hands of the patient according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint back together at its base, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension; and there are two administrators who extend the arm, and two who hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it; and when the master joins the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry dressing with egg white on top, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is firmly in place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not sit well, then start again with the poultice and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or place on the joint a piece of fat sheepskin, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then place the skin back on, and then into the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see [that it is not healing], place on top a moist warm cow's dung mixed with butter, and bind it up; thus will it return to its proper place.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than other joints. However, it must be brought back to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, lest the place become swollen or an abscess form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the reset is done thus: you place the injured hand on a table, and the attendant extends his hand, and the physician places it equally, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns. However, it is necessary to check if it is well in place; then the patient places the back of his hand on the table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the doctor should place his hand on top of that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is good. If not, then hold it with soothing poultices for these abscesses, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if the patient cannot bear it and you cannot put it in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted. And it does not harm the patient at all as long as the hand is moistened, and he cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries; and there is no other remedy except to apply cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have spoken of, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then soften it with hot water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on one side or the other, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then stretch the finger and push the dislocation towards you until it returns to its place, then support the head of the finger and pull it toward the side from which it was dislocated; leave it for 2 days, then make it equal that day; and bind it with a nut as we have said, and unbind it the next day, and move it, and rebind it with a nut; and do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, and do as you did before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine or neck is dislocated, and there are several such dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign is that the egestion jumps out of its place without will, and he cannot hold it back, and often some member is softened, either the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves in four parts; the part that moves at the rear is called "gibbosity": the cure for this is to reverse it if the gibbosity comes from childhood: there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or striking or similar things, the ancients spoke of cures in great words, where there is not always great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the case of jaundice which affects the chest first, there is neither wit nor health; and likewise in the case where it strikes both sides, and one cannot heal except for that which specifically affects the back, as I said; and let the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have support underneath him so he does not get hurt; then strike a taper into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the patient's buttocks, and another at the hips, and the knees, and the ankles; and two assistants should know how to handle the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two tapers; and they should be well tied, the tapers as we have said, and the doctor places his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board of three spans in length, and place it under the patient's back, and let the patient be on their side, and push the head of the board under the back, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the healer put their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that, do the same for the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you place two stakes at the patient's head one span apart, and towards the feet two others, and there should be between each stake a palm's length in height; and let there be a hole in each stake where the shoulder passes through, and let the stakes be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be a turning stake on which the rope turns, and between the two turning stakes there should be two small stakes a palm's length long for turning the shoulder; and then tie the rope that is among the pulleys to the shoulder towards the head, and the other rope to the other shoulder towards the feet, and let each of the assistants turn their stake all the way to the rope, and the master should make the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equalized, apply a drying plaster with plenty of egg, then the wool, and then a bandage from a tablet of three fingers in length, which should soak the place of the swelling and the healthy part of the vertebra, then bind with a ribbon as we have said, and let the patient use gentle nourishment until he is cured; and if anything comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines along with the bandage that we mentioned before; sometimes a piece of lead is applied, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower vertebrae of the back, and one might think it is dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, which is why one should not have presumption: by chance it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the hip and shoulder joints dislocation occurs alone, not like in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; more inside than otherwise, and little dislocation in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the sign of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the afflicted leg with the healthy one, it is longer and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee to the fire; and the place where the thigh bone goes there swells hot with abscess.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the signs of this occur when it happens to the contrary of those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the signs of this occur when it happens to the front, which is that one straightens his leg according to its fullness; however, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and the ankle swells, and when he walks, he goes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the signs of this occur when it happens to the back, which is that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The remedies for this type of dislocation are that you observe whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, in which case there is no cure; and it should not be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, then hasten to turn the joint, and place it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must have a strong assistant, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with one rope tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands under his heels, then pulls the rope gently on the thigh; and another holds the end of the rope; and they all pull up and down at the same time, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 This manner of extension is common to four types, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, then it is necessary to apply treatment according to its type When the dislocation is in the hip joint, it is necessary that you position the patient on his healthy side, then place the ligament on the root of the thigh, and the place that is below the buttock, then extend the ligament upwards towards the buttock, and towards the groin; then let another assistant take his arms, and embrace the large part of the sick thigh, and stretch it very strongly: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft ligature above the two ankles and above the two knees; and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him hang from the top of a stake, and let there be two arms' length above the ground. Then instruct one assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another assistant hanging with the patient strongly embrace the thigh, for the joint returns very quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is cured, let the patient lie down as we have said for those with gout, and tighten the ligature above the sick leg properly, and also above the foot; then place two splints, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a splint between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and let there be a planting of moist cloths around it so that it does not injure the patient. Then let each assistant lean towards him, and the physician place his hand equally with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on the table and press as we have said in the case of dislocation, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, as I have said; and let the physician place his hand on the affected ankle, then press with the other hand, and draw down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is behind, do not extend the affected leg downwards or lift it from the ground, but let it be as if the hip were dislocated behind, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let it lie on its side, and the ligament stretched as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends their legs, and they are equal; then bring the thighs together, and apply a poultice, and secure with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then unbind, and reapply the poultice; and if you see that they are equal, secure as before, and leave for three days; then unbind, and let it walk well, until the limb is comfortable. IENT
de la dislocation dou genoil	 of the knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
